Current Commentary

Opaque Outcome of the League of Nations Meeting 23

The League of Nations Administrative Council meeting. It commenced on the 21st of last month, followed by the Nineteen-Nation Committee and a Special Assembly. The Nineteen-Nation Committee was then entrusted with making recommendations. Aside from some back-and-forth procedures, the only thing of note was the fierce verbal battle between the Chinese and Japanese representatives. British Foreign Secretary Simon even sympathized with the Japanese representative and defended them. Although reports state that the British side has

repeatedly offered gentle explanations to our authorities, claiming that Simon's intention was to promote reconciliation and that he had no intention of favoring any party, the recent Nineteen-Nation Committee meeting shows no evidence to demonstrate his impartiality. The League of Nations is controlled by Britain and France, and although other small countries wish to uphold justice, they are too weak to make decisions. Even if they do, they cannot implement them. Therefore, in this Special Assembly, the four countries of Ireland, Spain, Czechoslovakia, and Sweden proposed the two items "Non-self-defense means of the September 18th Incident" and "Denial of Manchukuo," which were recognized by the Lytton Report, but were buried. The Five-Nation Subcommittee on Sino-Japanese Disputes (meeting for four weeks) not only disregarded China's upright justice but also dared not offend Japan, which was using barbarous force. Although the draft resolution it prepared has not been made public, the main points of the resolution can be divided into the following four points.

"1. The Conciliation Committee expresses its gratitude to the Lytton Commission for producing a report that provides sufficient reference and utilization."

"2. Confirmation of the League of Nations Assembly resolution of March 11 of this year."

"3. The Nineteen-Nation Committee should include representatives from both China and Japan to facilitate conciliation."

"4. Invite the United States and Russia, hoping that they will participate in the conciliation efforts."

The merits of the Nineteen-Nation Committee and the evaluation of the League of Nations are fully reflected in the above resolution. The Chinese people will henceforth have another renewed understanding and a profound lesson.

×××××

However, Britain and France are not completely unrelated to the Far East. Their diplomatic relations with our country are still considered friendly, and market competition with Japanese imperialism is particularly difficult to coordinate. Why have they gone from being bystanders to understanding Japan and attacking China?

Since Britain abandoned the gold standard on September 20 of last year, its credibility in the world financial market has declined. It is almost inevitable that it will try to recover in the future. Therefore, it first engaged in the reorganization of its internal affairs and organized a united national cabinet. Under this political system, income tax, consumption tax, and tariffs were increased, and the costs of social policies were reduced. In short, internally, the hardworking masses were sacrificed, and externally, colonies and semi-colonies were exploited to seek recovery.

After the balancing of the budget and the Ottawa British Empire Economic Conference, the British Empire became an economic unit on its own, implementing a closed-door policy and abandoning its traditional free trade policy, adopting a protective tariff system. As a result, it regained independence in financial policy and increased the cash reserves of the Bank of England. However, the war debt issue suddenly stirred up trouble, and rifts arose in the Anglo-French alliance. The difficulties of unemployment have not been resolved, and international disputes have suddenly become intense. Therefore, it has to resort to its old strategy of uniting with Japan in the East to seek security in the Far East and to stabilize the Chinese market.

××××

France has been rampant in the European continent for a lifetime. Since the world economic panic, it has suffered very little. Until recently, its financial market has also fallen into a state of congestion. Although gold reserves in the treasury have been increasing day by day, capital flow has been decreasing. Insufficient finances have led to the exhaustion of financial resources. All countries in the European continent are hoping to survive temporarily in the midst of storms. Therefore, the more cash France absorbs, the worse the international lending relationship becomes. In other words, after the implementation of high tariffs, imports are restricted, and the purchasing power of foreign countries is low, so export trade can only deteriorate. The pursuit of investment venues is France's top priority. The Soviet Union is one of its targets, and China in the Far East is particularly suitable. However, if it does not form a strong alliance with Japan, it will be difficult to ensure that its investment in China will not be actively hindered. Therefore, although France does not want Japan to swallow the Northeast alone, it is separated by geography and force, and it has no power to intervene.

××××

The United States of America was a nouveau riche after the European war. It wielded its financial power and reigned over East Asia. Our country's fatigue and Japan's tyranny made it difficult to oppose. However, under the influence of the decline of Europe for the past year, and the turbulence of the Jinnyang Incident, the panic has intensified. The number of unemployed people exceeds 10 million. Cash outflows are nearly 1 billion. The financial budget, in the four months from July to the present, has a revenue shortfall of more than 600 million US dollars. The state of its poverty can be imagined. It has no surplus power to oppose Japan.

××××

The Soviet Union is restoring normal diplomatic relations with our country and is focusing all its efforts on domestic construction. It is not a member of the League of Nations, so how can it take the blame for the League of Nations? Moreover, it still insists on its attitude of calm observation and will never speak out. Therefore, it also politely declined the invitation of the Nineteen-Nation Committee, knowing that the League of Nations cannot restrain Japan's atrocities. Moreover, are the Nineteen Committee still subordinate to the League of Nations? If it participates in mediation at this time, it will not help the matter and will only provoke criticism from the Japanese and arouse our country's antipathy.

××××

The powerlessness of the League of Nations has long been clear to the world. The situation of the great powers is also as described above. Whether it is Britain and France, which control Geneva diplomacy, or the United States and the Soviet Union, which stand outside the League of Nations, some want to share the spoils, some sigh in vain, and some are cold-eyed bystanders. None of them can alleviate our country's suffering. Can we continue to wait for the fair judgment of the League of Nations, which is forever impossible to expect, while being ravaged by Japanese warlords, without rising up to strive for self-reliance?

I still remember what the Central Party Headquarters said to the people in its book on September 18 of this year: "If there is reason to be spoken, speak reason. If there is no reason to be spoken, contend by force." In this special assembly of the League of Nations, we have exhausted our last loyalty and spoken reason with tears and blood. What is the result? Not only is there no reason to be spoken, but there is no way to speak any further. From now on, is there any other way besides "contending by force?"

The Resolution Drafted by the League of Nations Subcommittee is Vague and Ambiguous 24

Recalling the March 11 Resolution to Organize a Conciliation Committee and Invite China, Japan, the United States, and Russia to Participate

Expressing Gratitude to the Investigative Commission and Suggesting the Lytton Report as a Basis for Conciliation

Leaving Room for Japan to Quibble

British Foreign Secretary Simon's Pro-Japan Bias is Obvious

No Deadline for Resolution is Specified

Chinese and Japanese Representatives Request Instructions from Their Respective Governments

(Geneva) The draft resolution prepared by the Subcommittee of the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee is quite vague and ambiguous due to the influence of Britain's pro-Japan bias, as if to leave room for Japan to quibble. If British Foreign Secretary Simon had not returned to London on Wednesday, the results would have been even worse. According to a report from a reporter from the Central News Agency, the initial draft of the Subcommittee only stipulated that the basis for conciliation would be the League of Nations Covenant and the Kellogg-Briand Pact for resolving disputes by peaceful means, but did not include the Nine-Power Treaty, which clearly guaranteed China's territorial and administrative integrity. Only after a request from our country's representative was it added. Furthermore, the draft resolution did not specify a time limit for resolution, only stating that the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee should report on the results of conciliation to the Assembly by March 1 of next year, rather than submit recommendations. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 16th)

(Geneva) It is reported that the draft resolution approved by the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee on the evening of the 15th contains four items: (1) Expressing admiration for the work of the Lytton Commission and using its report in the work of the Conciliation Committee; (2) Reaffirming the resolution of March 11; (3) Proposing that the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee serve as the Conciliation Committee, supplemented by representatives from China and Japan; (4) Suggesting that the United States and Russia be invited to participate in the conciliation efforts. (Reuters Dispatch, 15th)

(Geneva) The draft resolution prepared by the Subcommittee of the Nineteen-Nation Committee has been completed today and sent to the leaders of the Chinese and Japanese delegations for review. After obtaining their consent, it will be submitted to the League of Nations Assembly. As for its content, although the members of the committee are trying to keep it secret, reliable sources say that this resolution is relatively vague and does not assume any responsibility, and the committee may have to try to draft it again.

It is also reported that the Nineteen-Nation Committee held a meeting for a short time today and passed three documents drafted by the Subcommittee, preparing to submit them to the League of Nations Assembly after obtaining the consent of China and Japan.

(The first document) is to suggest the aforementioned draft resolution. Its content mainly consists of the League of Nations Assembly reiterating the outline of the resolution of the last Assembly on March 11, and each member state guaranteeing that it will not recognize any situation or treaty produced by means that violate the Covenant and the Pact of Paris. Secondly, it focuses on the conditions of the Covenant, the Pact of Paris, and the Nine-Power Treaty. Thirdly, it suggests the establishment of a Conciliation Committee, with the Nineteen-Nation Committee as members, and adding the two countries involved, China and Japan. The United States and Russia, because they have significant interests in the Far East, should also be invited to participate. This Conciliation Committee should consider Chapters 9 and 10 of the Lytton Report and submit a report on March 1 of next year.

(The second document) is said to be quite short, only expressing gratitude for the impartial work of the Lytton Commission.

(The third document) is two pages long and details the reasons for the Nineteen-Nation Committee drafting the resolution. In this report, it is strongly argued that the League of Nations Assembly should adopt conciliation measures in accordance with Article 15, Section 3 of the Covenant, and explain the need to invite the United States and Russia to participate in conciliation. It is said that the historical part of the Lytton Report on the Manchurian case is unbiased, and that both advocating a return to the original state and recognizing "Manchukuo" are impossible. Therefore, it is necessary to find some compromise solutions.

It is also reported that the attitude of people in the League of Nations is to hope that the final resolution of the League of Nations Assembly will be sufficiently vague and not assume any responsibility, in order to please Japan, so that the Japanese can continue to participate in the conciliation work. However, the resolution of the committee should be slightly tougher, and it can ignore the approval of the League of Nations Assembly, in order to please China and obtain the cooperation of the United States and Russia. (National Telegram, 15th)

(Geneva) The Chairman of the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee claimed to people today that very active negotiations are underway to seek an agreement on the organization of the conciliation mechanism for handling the Sino-Japanese dispute. The governments of the United States and Russia will be invited to join this mechanism. After the meeting of the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee yesterday, he met with the Secretary-General of the League of Nations to inquire about the opinions of the Chinese and Japanese representatives on this method. He has contacted both parties on this matter and is now awaiting the replies from the two governments. The League of Nations Assembly is likely to be delayed for several days before it can convene. (Reuters Dispatch, 16th)

(Geneva) The resolution passed by the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee yesterday was checked for the number of copies and sealed after the meeting, which proves the secrecy of the meeting. It is reported that the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee suggested that the committee be the Conciliation Committee, supplemented by representatives from China and Japan. The committee should submit a report to the League of Nations within six months. Dr. Yan Huiqing has advocated this point for several months, believing that if conciliation is ineffective within the specified period, the Conciliation Committee should prepare a report, and there may be proposals for sanctions at that time. The conciliation methods contained in Chapters 9 and 10 of the Lytton Report should have a chance of success. The Nineteen-Nation Special Committee decided not to express any opinions on the merits of the dispute, in order to avoid any suspicion of favoritism, but will reaffirm the resolution of March 11, not recognizing changes made in violation of the Covenant. This move is to satisfy the small countries, as the small countries have reluctantly abandoned the claim of not recognizing "Manchukuo". The League of Nations Assembly will likely convene on Monday or Tuesday of next week to discuss this resolution. It is expected that after this meeting, the entire issue will be postponed to next year for further handling. (Reuters Dispatch, 16th)

(Geneva) Regarding the work of the Drafting Committee, the following is a continuation of the news. The Drafting Committee has passed two resolutions and one statement of reasons yesterday, and the first part of its work has been completed. The principles on which the conciliation of the Sino-Japanese dispute should be based have also been determined. As for the conciliation procedure, the Drafting Committee advocates organizing a small committee, with experts and specially qualified people as members, which may refer to the members of the Lytton Commission, but it is not certain. The Drafting Committee also suggested that the Extraordinary Assembly should invite the United States and Russia to participate. The Nineteen-Nation Committee was therefore reorganized into a Twenty-One-Nation Committee. According to the League of Nations Covenant, the final report on the Sino-Japanese dispute should be published within six months. Later, the Extraordinary Assembly decided to postpone it. The Chinese representative repeatedly requested a definite deadline for publication. The above statement of reasons is to satisfy the Chinese side's request. The statement said that the Conciliation Committee should determine the deadline for submitting the final report by the end of this year. If the work of the Conciliation Committee is completed, the final report will only describe the facts of the case. If the conciliation fails, the final report will include various proposals. As for the principles on which the conciliation work should be based, according to the statement of reasons, the League of Nations Covenant, the Pact of Paris, and the Washington Nine-Power Treaty should be given the most attention. Then, it recalls the resolution of the Assembly on March 11, which does not recognize the situation created by violence. It also describes Chapter 9 of the Lytton Report on the principles of conciliation and Chapter 10 on the methods of conciliation. Chapter 9 of the Lytton Report recommends granting extensive autonomy to Manchuria, organizing a gendarmerie, withdrawing all other troops, and building China through international cooperation. Chapter 10 of the Lytton Report proposes convening a consultation meeting, with representatives from both China and Japan and two groups of representatives of residents of Manchuria participating. One group of representatives is elected by the method prescribed by China, and the other is elected by the method prescribed by Japan. In addition, neutral observers can also participate in the meeting. If there are different opinions, the Executive Council of the League of Nations should resolve them. The statement of reasons also stated that all the proposed methods are based on Article 15, Section 3 of the Covenant. The reason for not making any judgments is that the conciliation work must be free to use. (Havas Dispatch, 16th)

Intention to Delay the Resolution of the Sino-Japanese Dispute

Merely Becoming a Mechanism for Japan and the Great Powers

(Geneva) The League of Nations' intention to delay the resolution of the Sino-Japanese dispute is undeniable. The League of Nations has merely become the League of Nations of Japan and the Great Powers. Japan needs to delay to complete its plan in the three eastern provinces. The League of Nations, hopeless from the beginning, also welcomes the delay to preserve its face. As for the Great Powers, in order to avoid Japan's resistance, they also believe that it is better to let it develop naturally, resolving it without resolving it. Under this situation, our country cannot even obtain a satisfactory resolution on paper. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 16th)

Our Delegation Disappointed with the Resolution 26

Completely Following Japan's Intentions

(Geneva) The Chinese delegation is very disappointed with the draft submitted by the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee to the Assembly. Furthermore, there are no provisions in the draft to deal with the situation in the three eastern provinces, nor are there any measures to prevent Japan from continuing its aggression. Japan Still Shows Dissatisfaction 27

Opposes the Participation of the United States and Russia

Continues to Use Intimidation Tactics

(Tokyo) The Japanese representatives, including Representative Matsuoka, will immediately request instructions from their home government regarding the results of the Nineteen-Nation Committee. After discussion, the representatives believed that the adoption of the Lytton Report meant not recognizing "Manchukuo", so they unanimously opposed it. The British representative Simon's comforting speech at the Nineteen-Nation Committee on the 15th had the opposite effect, resulting in a more unfavorable situation for Japan. The Japanese representatives have prepared for all contingencies and decided that there is no other option but to withdraw from the League of Nations. (Japan League Telegram, 16th)

(Tokyo) The intentions of the Japanese Army authorities regarding the resolution of the Nineteen-Nation Committee are as follows: The Army has only received the previous article, and the entire text has not yet been received. The Army is absolutely opposed to declaring that the Lytton Report is accepted, which means not recognizing the Liutiao Lake Incident as an act of self-defense. Furthermore, the adoption of the March 11 resolution means that Japan's actions violated the Pact of Paris, the League of Nations Covenant, and the Nine-Power Treaty, so it cannot be approved either. Furthermore, regarding the invitation of the United States and Russia, it is necessary to oppose Russia's participation today when China and Russia have restored diplomatic relations. Furthermore, the government will consult with the Army and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs after the full text arrives,

and then instruct Plenipotentiary Matsuoka. (Dentsu Dispatch, 16th)

The Result of the German Reichstag Re-election (German Correspondence) Public Safety 77

The re-election of the German Reichstag, again held on October 6th, although inevitably slightly affected by the Berlin transport workers' strike beforehand, was generally orderly and stable. Fortunately, there were no major clashes, bloodshed, or tragic election dramas. The results of this Reichstag re-election, the distribution of votes and seats, are as follows:

Party Votes Seats

National Socialist Workers' Party 11,713,785 195

Social Democratic Party 7,237,894 121

German Communist Party 5,974,209 100

Centre Party 4,228,633 69

German National People's Party 3,064,977 51

Bavarian People's Party 1,081,932 19

German People's Party 660,092 11

German State Party 338,064 2

Christian Social People's Service Party 412,685 5

Economic Party 110,181 2

German Farmers' Party 148,990 3

Others 436,866 4

Total 35,402,306 577

In terms of the number of votes, the number of voters in this election decreased by 5% compared to the previous election. In terms of the number of seats, the previous election produced 607 members, while this time there were only 577, a decrease of 30, which is a matter of great concern. The reason for this is, on the one hand, that the people are tired of elections, a phenomenon known as "Wahlmüdigkeit" (election fatigue). Since the last five months, the German people have experienced 13 major elections and 700 minor elections, and the people are overwhelmed by the frequency. Therefore, many passive citizens gave up their right to vote this time. This fact was anticipated by German public opinion, so it is not surprising. Furthermore, dissecting and observing the election results of each faction, the National Socialist Labor Party, occupying 195 seats, still holds the leading position among the parliamentary parties, but compared to the election results three months ago, its voter numbers have sharply declined, suffering a tremendous defeat. Hitler must be discouraged. Hitler's fascist movement has suffered a fatal blow, and it is not impossible that it will disintegrate as a result. When the results of the previous July 31st

Reichstag election were announced, British, French, American, and Russian public opinion all made direct and clear judgments, stating that the German fascist movement had reached its peak and would not make any further progress in the future. Their predictions were accurate. The reasons for this failure are extremely complex, but to summarize, there are approximately the following main reasons:

(1) The people gradually realized that Hitler's claims were mostly hollow and impractical.

(2) Hitler's economic policies became increasingly communist, losing the support of the middle class.

(3) The Lausanne Conference's acceptance of Germany's request to suspend reparations eased the German xenophobia.

(4) Hitler's party members were too rampant, constantly clashing with the Communist Party, resulting in bloody tragedies, causing social unrest, and arousing hatred among the people.

(5) After Hitler's failure in the presidential and July 31st Reichstag election campaigns, his energy waned, and the tide of the movement receded.

With these five reasons, the decline of fascism is inevitable. The Social Democratic Party, due to its relatively moderate and stable attitude, also slightly declined in this election compared to the previous election, but it is still the second most important party in the Reichstag. The Centre Party, since the collapse of the Brüning cabinet, has seen its political power decline. In addition, Brüning and Papen within the party have disagreed, showing signs of disintegration. Furthermore, without concrete solutions and proposals for the current economic panic and unemployment problems in Germany, the party's value has gradually diminished. Therefore, in this Reichstag election, it only obtained 69 seats. However, the far-left German Communist Party, in this Reichstag election, saw a surprisingly rapid increase in voter numbers. It can also be said to be the party that achieved the greatest victory in this Reichstag election, occupying 100 seats in the Reichstag and becoming the third most important party. The surge in the Communist Party's votes this time has posed a tremendous threat to the far-right National Socialist Labor Party. In world public opinion and politics, it cannot but attract attention. The reasons for the increase in the Communist Party's votes are, firstly, due to the economic panic and the problem of unemployed workers in Germany, and secondly, due to the increasing development and tension of anti-capitalist and world revolution ideologies.

Now that the new Reichstag has been re-elected, and the distribution of seats is as mentioned above, no single party, from the far left to the far right, has been able to obtain an absolute majority of seats in the parliament. Then, how will the so-called majority faction of the parliamentary government be formed and produced? This Reichstag re-election has produced 577 members. To be an absolute majority, 289 members are needed. The National Socialist Labor Party only has 195 members, which is of course far from that number. It is unable to become the absolute majority faction in the parliament on its own. The left-wing Communist Party and the Social Democratic Party combined have 221 members, which is a greater force than the right-wing. However, they still do not meet the qualifications for an absolute majority faction in the parliament. Only the Communist Party can cooperate with the right-wing, i.e., the National Socialist Labor Party, to obtain 295 members and form an absolute majority faction. However, in the end, these two parties, one turning to the left and the other running to the right, are diametrically opposed, and their opinions are as incompatible as ice and charcoal. It is extremely difficult to believe that cats and mice can cooperate. In conclusion, it can be seen that the formation of the new German Reichstag and the problem of the government's majority faction are just as difficult as the situation in the Reichstag elected on July 31st. The future is very grey and bleak.

The reason why Papen previously dissolved the Reichstag elected on July 31st was precisely because the Reichstag could not form an absolute majority faction in the government. If the newly re-elected Reichstag still cannot form an absolute majority faction in the government, then how will the Papen cabinet deal with it? If Papen cannot find a proper solution to this problem, then the fate of his cabinet cannot but be doomed to collapse due to the Reichstag re-election. On the eve of this Reichstag re-election, Papen gave an extremely solemn election speech to the entire German nation through loudspeakers, and clearly expressed his abandonment of his consistent pro-right attitude, strongly criticizing the inappropriate behavior of the right and left parties, and proposing a new proposition, the so-called supra-party politics. He believes that in Germany's current extremely dangerous and impoverished situation, fragmented and divisive political parties are of no help in overcoming difficulties. The only way out for saving the country in the future is for all Germans to take the overall interests of the nation and the country as the premise, stand on the same front and group, and be directed by the meritorious President Hindenburg, so that the practical effect of saving the country can be achieved. In other words, Papen's view is that the future Reichstag should move away from the direction of partisan divisions and form a supra-party coalition parliamentary government majority faction. This so-called supra-party coalition work problem is also deeply sympathized with by current public opinion, forming the core and focus of the newly elected Reichstag. However, there is little hope that this new proposition of Papen will be accepted by the various political parties. Because of his speech on the eve of this Reichstag re-election, which greatly attacked the right and left factions, he aroused extreme resentment from the Communist Party and Hitler's party members, to the extent that they had to overthrow the Papen cabinet immediately. Therefore, almost all of the newly elected Reichstag members are opposed to Papen, and can also be said to be anti-government. With such thorny difficulties, it is thought that Papen will not easily break through them. On Papen's side, there is the protective talisman of Article 48 of the National Constitution to preserve his position. When the Reichstag cannot form a government majority faction or when there are other difficult problems that cannot be resolved, Article 48 of the National Constitution can be applied, and the Reichstag can be ordered to be dissolved and re-elected. It should be known that since Papen took office as the premier of the cabinet, he has twice ordered the dissolution of the Reichstag due to the parliament's vote of no confidence. The people cannot bear the frequency of elections, and from an economic point of view, the two elections have cost a total of 77 million marks. Therefore, the more elections there are, the greater the burden on the people. If Papen still wants to use this constitutional provision as a talisman to deal with the Reichstag and protect himself, he may eventually provoke actual revolutionary actions by the various parties and plunge the political situation into greater unrest. Papen has now decided to consult with President Hindenburg in two weeks to determine his attitude and steps towards the new Reichstag. The opening date of the new Reichstag, according to constitutional regulations, should be held within one month after the election. The official announcement of this matter, as of the time the reporter took up his pen, has not yet been made, but public opinion speculates that the first meeting of the new Reichstag will be convened on December 6th, in Freiburg, Germany.

Japan to Armedly Survey Land Maps for the Northeast Army 78

On the Other Hand, the Ministry of Education Revised the Puppet State Textbooks

From This, It Can Be Seen That Japan's Ambitions Are Progressing Step by Step

The Nagasaki Daily News says, "The map of Manchuria" was originally a military map obtained from Russia during the Russo-Japanese War. Later, based on this map, a rough estimate of its area and terrain was made. However, in reality, it is quite incomplete. Now, taking advantage of the opportunity of Manchuria's independence, there is a need to create a detailed military map. The Survey Department of the Army General Staff has repeatedly discussed the matter carefully with the leadership and is now ready. It has selected survey technicians who are proficient in the geography of Manchuria and will send them to conduct actual surveys under armed escort. On the other hand, the Ministry of Education has decided to revise the geography textbooks for higher elementary schools in "Manchuria" starting from the new semester in April next year. The content records an area of 1.1 million square miles and a population of 35 million people. In addition, in order to explore the resources and the mysterious endless treasures of the region, survey personnel, under armed escort by the Kwantung Army, are dispatched to various places. In places where forests and mountains cannot be traversed by human power, lighter-than-air balloons and airplanes are used for three-dimensional surveying. According to Lieutenant Colonel Matsuoka of the General Staff, the completion of a Japanese map takes 38 years. The map of Manchuria requires 50 years to complete a detailed investigation and survey.

Major Fire in a Department Store in Tokyo 88

Burned for Four Hours, More Than Ten Dead and Over a Hundred Injured

Half of the Eight-Story Building Destroyed, Losses of Five Million

Five Army Aircraft Busy Rescuing People

Reuters, Tokyo, 16th - This morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the eight-story Shirokiya Department Store here. For a time, flames shot out and thick smoke rose. Firefighters worked hard to rescue the hundreds of people trapped inside the store, and the army, armed with bayonet-tipped guns, assisted the police in clearing the crowd of onlookers nearby. The fire started on the third floor and spread upwards. The customers in the store were all panicked, mostly women and children. It is reported that the fire started in the section of old Christmas incense toys. Customers and female shop assistants on the upper floors ran to the roof garden, shouting for help. It is reported that three people jumped from the sixth-floor windows and fell to their deaths on the road. At that time, army aircraft dropped life-saving equipment on the roof garden to rescue those trapped there.

Continued Telegram - The fire at the Shirokiya Department Store burned for three and a half hours before it was extinguished. It is reported that a total of ten people died and over a hundred were injured, with about fifty people seriously injured. The amount of loss is approximately 5 million yen. When the fire was raging, the two lions kept in the animal enclosure on the roof garden also tried to escape, causing even more panic among the crowd.

Dentsu, Tokyo, 16th - Due to the fire at Shirokiya, as of noon, it has been confirmed that the number of deaths has reached eleven. Firefighters and police are still cooperating to search the burnt remains, and the number of deaths may still increase.

Dentsu, Tokyo, 16th - The cause of the fire at Shirokiya is currently under investigation. It seems to be near the toys sold before Christmas on the fourth floor, where the electric light wire was damaged and leaked electricity, causing the fire. The fourth, fifth, sixth, and seventh floors have all been burned. However, the forty or fifty customers who took refuge on the roof were rescued. Among the seventy female servants in the dining hall, thirty were rescued, and the remaining forty are feared to have died or been injured. Also, of the seventy seriously injured people admitted to Nihonbashi Hospital at 11:00 AM, six have died. Because the door was opened for rescue and the fire started immediately afterwards, there were relatively few customers. If it had been at noon, there would have been more deaths and injuries.

Japan Alliance News Agency, Tokyo, 16th - After the fire at Shirokiya, the police used their best efforts to rescue the shop assistants above the third floor. This work was quite difficult, so they requested the army to send aircraft for rescue. Five army aircraft were dispatched at 11:00 AM, dropped long ropes from the air, and began rescuing people. By 12:50 PM, seven people had died and ninety were injured.

There Was Also a Fire in Hachinohe City, Japan 89

Dentsu Agency, Hachinohe, 16th - At 3:55 PM today, a fire broke out at the Rui'e Izumiyama residential office in Hachinohe City, Aomori Prefecture. At that time, due to the strong wind, the fire was very fierce, destroying thirty houses. The fire was extinguished at 5:30 PM. War Debts Due, Large Batch of Gold Bars Shipped to the US

Six Countries Paid, Five Did Not 90

Reuters, Washington, 15th - The countries that paid their debts today include England, Italy, Czechoslovakia, Finland, Latvia, and Lithuania, totaling US$125 million. The countries that did not pay their debts are France, Belgium, Poland, Estonia, and Hungary, owing a total of US$25 million.

Kokumin, London, 15th - This morning, the Bank of England marked gold bars worth £19,750,000, indicating that they now belong to the Federal Reserve Bank of New York in the United States, as payment for the British war debt due to the United States today. The transportation procedures are currently being prepared by brokers. Because insurance companies are currently unwilling to guarantee huge amounts of money, it will probably be shipped in more than ten shipments. The Bank of England also stated today that after selling gold bars worth £19,632,831 to the government, the current gold reserves are £120,672,169.

Kokumin, Washington, 15th - US Treasury Secretary Mills stated that after France, Belgium, and other countries defaulted on their war debts, although it would increase the treasury deficit for this fiscal year, there was no way to do anything about it. As for the business relationship with France, Belgium, and other countries, it will continue as usual. For example, Russia has not paid a single cent to its creditors, but various countries continue to do business with it as usual. According to the twelve debtor countries, it is hoped that nine countries will pay all or part of their debts today. Even Lithuania paid US$92,386.01 in gold yuan with a check from a bank in Washington, DC. Although there has been some reaction in the US Congress to the default on war debts, such as Senator McKellar's proposal to levy a passport fee of $5,000 each time to force travelers not to enter debtor countries, and Congressman Mansfield also made a similar proposal, it is expected that it will not be discussed immediately.

Havas, Romanian Capital, 15th - The grace period for Eastern European countries to receive Eastern reparations expired today. Romania has recently agreed to extend the grace period by six months and has notified the International Clearing Bank of this matter. Romania has obtained an exchange condition for this concession, that is, the UK and France have agreed to extend the grace period for Romania's debts to them by six months.

Kokumin, Warsaw, 15th - The political circles here have been deeply impressed by the French Parliament's refusal to repay the US war debt. The Polish government is now asking the United States for a grace period for the war debt. If this request is rejected by the United States, the Polish government will resolutely refuse to pay the debt due in November, following the example of France. The Polish government has expressed its willingness to discuss with the United States how to determine a solution to the war debt problem, but given the current economic difficulties, it is impossible to immediately repay the 27 million zlotys (Polish currency) due in December.

Kokumin, Prague, 15th - The Czechoslovak government has paid US$1.5 million in gold yuan for the US war debt due in December.

Kokumin, Lithuanian Capital, 15th - The Lithuanian government has paid the US war debt due in December today, totaling US$91,000 in US treasury bonds. Lithuania had previously requested a grace period, but it was not approved by the United States.

Germany Strives for Revival

Schleicher Announces Political Program 91

Large-Scale Re-Agriculturalization Plan

Restore Conscription System to Train Youth

Kokumin, Berlin, 15th - Prime Minister Schleicher said in a radio speech tonight that he neither supports capitalism nor socialism, because these doctrines, in the strict sense, no longer exist and have lost their appeal in economic life.

Oppose Military Dictatorship 92

Schleicher said that he was apprehensive when he was appointed, because being appointed as Prime Minister from the position of Minister of Defense can easily lead people to suspect that he wants to establish a military dictatorship. Therefore, he asked the people not to regard him as a soldier, but as someone entrusted with the interests of people from all walks of life, so that they can overcome the short-term difficulties.

Seeking Work for the People 93

As for the government's administrative policy, in a word, it is to seek work for the people, because this is what the people are most concerned about. As for amending the constitution and other good things that cannot stop hunger, they are not what the government wants. Only the revival of commerce can end the panic of unemployment. However, it is useless to comfort the people with empty words, saying that after a famine year, there will be a bumper year. Therefore, the cabinet is currently drafting a great plan to seek work for the people.

The cabinet will also avoid inflation, not levy new taxes in the next fiscal year, and not reduce official salaries and wages again.

Focus on Developing Agriculture 94

Developing agriculture is also an essential plan for relieving unemployment. Next year, an initial appropriation of 50 million marks will be used to relocate immigrants to Eastern Prussia and other places, followed by another appropriation of 50 million marks, which will be provided by the German Bank. The main reason for the suffering of Germany and the world is that there are few farmers and many people making a living in cities. It is now urgent to remedy this shortcoming, but it will take at least thirty years to achieve success. The cabinet will first operate to revitalize the domestic market, but the foreign market should also be given importance. The previous Papen cabinet had already started this undertaking, and this cabinet will inherit its legacy. The previous cabinet's measures to help farmers will also be vigorously promoted.

Private enterprises and state enterprises are currently mixed and unclear, causing many harms. The cabinet will now pay special attention to this matter to make the boundaries clear so that each can benefit.

The parliament has recently cancelled some of the stricter provisions in the emergency decree issued on September 4th. The cabinet has actually assisted in this.

Alleviate the Suffering of Unemployment 95

The suffering of millions of unemployed people cannot be relieved in a few months, but he must do his best to alleviate it. Schleicher then enumerated several of the temporary relief plans that are currently being considered for implementation, such as reducing the price of meat and coal, and may also reduce the price of milk and bread.

Curb Terrorism 96

Schleicher continued by saying that emergency plans to curb political terrorism cannot be used to govern the country all the time, so he has asked the President to cancel it. If there are still people who do not know themselves and have extraordinary actions, the government will still issue strict orders to govern the chaos. Schleicher then issued a warning to the Communist Party.

Restore Conscription 97

Schleicher then touched on the issue of youth training, saying that parents and teachers have recently sent him sincere letters urging him to restore conscription. There is nothing better than this system for enabling young people to learn the ways of self-government, humility, and friendship. My repeated advocacy of using conscription to train militias is for this main reason.

Demanding Armament 98

Subsequently, regarding Germany's position on the issue of disarmament, he said that he often solemnly declared that our country is prepared to supply the army with lead knives and paper quality, as long as neighboring countries do the same. Otherwise, the Germans are also unwilling to let their heads be cut off by others, so they demand that their national defense forces should guarantee the same security as other countries. The Italian government has always supported our people's demand for equal rights. This is what Germany

The people should be sincerely grateful for this. The German government will respond to the work arising from the current situation with calm determination and perseverance, and is prepared to work sincerely with the governments of all countries that have the will to solve international problems with justice and good faith understanding.

The Spirit of Country First, Party Second 100

Therefore, if they only do nothing and are fond of petty tricks, the people's hearts will turn away from them.

Havas, Paris, 15th: President Lebrun continues to seek opinions from various parties to resolve the cabinet crisis. The President then entrusted Shao Dan, a member of the Radical Socialist Party and former mayor, to try to form a cabinet. Shao requested time to respond tomorrow.

The Northeast Problem and the League of Nations (3) 103

Participation of the Investigation Team

Verbal Battles Between Chinese and Japanese Representatives

Furthermore, the Chinese representative, while in Changchun, sent a document to the Investigation Team on May 3 regarding the interference by Japanese police he encountered when meeting with two foreign teachers at the Yamato Hotel. One section reads as follows: "Upon opening the door, five or six Japanese individuals were seen, with one leading man insistently trying to enter the room to investigate the identity of the visitors and the purpose of their visit. It was later learned that this Japanese individual was the chief of the Changchun Police Department of the Kwantung Leased Territory. After entering the room, he did not leave until the Chinese representative stepped out of his private chamber. At this time, Mr. Esde, a member of the Investigation Team, happened to pass by and inquired of the Japanese police chief, who revealed that he wanted to know if the Chinese representative had obtained permission from the Japanese police to meet with foreign guests, and whether these foreign guests had also obtained permission from the Japanese police to visit the Chinese representative." When the Chinese representative was in Jilin, he was "escorted" everywhere by Japanese soldiers carrying rifles with bayonets. In Harbin, he was "escorted" by uniformed and plainclothes Japanese police officers. Due to these inappropriate restrictions and prohibitions, the Chinese representative was unable to accompany the Investigation Team to the scene of incidents to investigate everything or to present Chinese witnesses for the Investigation Team's interviews. Chinese people in the Three Eastern Provinces were absolutely not allowed to meet with the Investigation Team or Chinese representatives without the permission of the Japanese authorities. Report 107 states, "However, the result of various methods by the Japanese police was only to isolate all witnesses. Many Chinese were even afraid to meet with members of the Investigation Team. The Investigation Team learned in one place that before its arrival, the authorities had announced that no one could meet with the Investigation Team without official approval. Therefore, all visits by the Investigation Team were conducted secretly, with great difficulty, and many people found this secret meeting method to be dangerous. Most of the delegations received by the Investigation Team were introduced by the Japanese authorities or the 'Manchukuo' authorities. The members of the committee firmly believe that their written opinions must have been approved by Japan beforehand." The treatment of the Chinese representative and his staff by the Japanese authorities in the Three Eastern Provinces, a part of Chinese territory, contrasted sharply with the immense freedom and convenience granted to the Japanese representative by the Chinese authorities in other parts of China. The Chinese authorities never attempted in any way to hinder the Japanese representative from presenting Japanese witnesses or Japanese people to the Investigation Team to offer their opinions when the Investigation Team was in Nanjing, Shanghai, Hankou, Beiping, and other places. The above points are merely a preliminary indication. Now, I will express my opinion on a few of the more important issues and facts presented in the report.

The Japanese government has claimed that China is not an organized nation. While this statement superficially defends Japan's improper actions in China, especially in the Three Eastern Provinces, its true purpose is to confuse public opinion and avoid the real issues. China is one of the original member states of the League of Nations. For the Japanese government to address it with such disparaging terms shows a lack of accumulation and reveals that the Japanese side has absolutely no sound justification for its arguments in this case. China is currently in the process of transforming from a four-thousand-year-old imperial system to a modern democratic system. The various difficulties it faces are not surprising to anyone familiar with the political history of national transformations. The various complex forces and factors within China are merely manifestations of the power and vitality of the awakened Chinese nation and a testament to the progress of the nation on which the livelihood of 450 million people depends. The phenomena in China's transition process may not be entirely satisfactory to outside observers, but these phenomena are common in any renovation process of an old structure. The most important point is what is stated in the seventeenth section of the Investigation Team's report: "Despite various difficulties, delays, and failures, the Chinese government has achieved quite a bit."

Inspection Notes on Suppressing Communists and Recovering Various Areas (2)

Refugees Gradually Gather in Yuekou 104

Yuekou is an important town in the central area of Hubei Province, located on the Xiang River. Communist suppression military operations are centered here. In August 1930, it was occupied by the Red Army for three days, resulting in burning, killing, looting, and losses of over two million. Although it was later recovered by the National Army, the surrounding areas were rampant with bandits, causing the people to live in insecurity, businesses to decline, and rural areas to be destroyed. The original vitality has not yet been restored. At that time, the southern bank of the Xiang River was entirely occupied by bandits. The National Army and the bandits confronted each other across the river for a long time, engaging in bloody battles before finally driving back the bandits, advancing on Qianjiang, and directly attacking Honghu. Currently, Yuekou is the defense area of the Tenth Army. The General Headquarters and the Tenth Army Headquarters are located here. A special service regiment is stationed here. Local order is maintained jointly by the military and police. The militia organization uses spears and broadswords as weapons and does not have modern firearms. There are about eight battalions with over a thousand men. The people's self-defense organization is already taking shape. If further training and replenishment of firearms are provided, the people will be able to defend themselves against bandits and clear the countryside. A household survey was conducted once after the bandits were driven back. Currently, refugees are gradually gathering, and preparations for the Baojia system are underway. As for rural cooperation, it has not yet been implemented due to time constraints. In terms of education, there were several primary schools, but after the bandit disaster, they are barely maintaining the status quo. In addition to postal and telecommunications services, long-distance buses, thanks to the Tenth Army's efforts in building roads, connect to Hankou in the east, Shashi in the west, and Qianjiang in the south, which is extremely convenient. The road from Yuekou to Qianjiang is open to traffic today. The section from Yuekou to Shashi is being rushed to be repaired and will also be directly accessible tomorrow. The reporter arrived in Yuekou last night (the 8th) and took a bus to Qianjiang this morning at 10 AM for inspection.

Tragic Situation After the Bandit Disaster in Qianjiang 105

Qianjiang is located near Honghu, bordering Tianmen and Yingcheng to the north, Mianyang to the east, and Jianli and Jiangling to the southwest. Its strategic location made it the base for bandits entrenched in Honghu to expand outwards. In August 1930, He Long led his troops into Qianjiang City, implementing communization and redistributing land, allocating two mu of land to each person. The people lived in insecurity, and much of the land was barren. Moreover, the bandits engaged in terrible burning and killing, with most of the houses in the surrounding countryside being burned and demolished. In the city, in addition to the county government, party headquarters, and churches being burned down, countless civilian houses were also destroyed. Those that were not completely destroyed had most of their doors and windows torn down. As for the residents' possessions, they were almost completely taken away. The bandits used Honghu as their base, and lacking building materials in the lake, they dismantled houses in Qianjiang and used the materials to build their bandit nests. The county government has not yet been repaired and is temporarily using a dilapidated academy as its office. The party headquarters and churches are temporarily renting civilian houses. The remaining shops and residences are repaired and occupied with reeds and mud, creating a dilapidated scene that is unbearable to witness. The bandit massacres in Qianjiang are horrific. The methods of killing are even more unexpected. In addition to beheading, the types of punishment included confiscation (a special bandit term meaning burial alive), eye gouging, military conscription, drowning, guillotine execution, sawing, and dismemberment. Those who were confiscated were secretly tied up and ordered to dig their own pits, placed upside down in the pits, and covered with soil. The families of the killed only knew that they were missing and did not know they were killed, let alone find their bodies. The number of people confiscated in the city and countryside is countless. Those who were eye-gouged had their eyes gouged out while still alive. The bandits often gouged out the eyes of their victims before executing them, and many died in this way. Military conscription involved covering the head with black cloth, leaving only the eyes exposed, so that outsiders could not recognize the true face. Those who were conscripted lightly were exiled to other places, while those who were heavily conscripted were taken to remote areas and killed. Those who were drowned were thrown into the lake, and the bandits threw stones at them from the shore until they were dead. Guillotine execution involved cutting the victim in half at the waist. Sawing involved using wooden boards to clamp the victim upright and sawing them in half from the crotch to the heel. Dismemberment involved dividing the body into several pieces after killing and scattering them in all directions. Such brutal and inhumane massacres are unheard of. The National Army and the bandits entered and exited Qianjiang more than ten times. It is estimated that over ten thousand residents were killed in the city, and even more in the surrounding countryside. It is estimated that four or five tenths of the people in the city died, and five or six tenths of the people in the surrounding countryside died. There was a female bandit named Qian Ying, originally a widow. Her family forced her to remarry, but Ying fled to Russia, embraced celibacy, and returned to China to serve as a member of the Communist Party Central Committee. She was brutal and killed countless people. This autumn, she was killed by the National Army in Zhoujiazu, and the rumor that He Long's sister, He Ying, was killed was a mistake for Qian Ying. The National Army recovered Qianjiang on July 14 this year and attacked Honghu, encircling it on all sides. As the army advanced deep, the bandits were finally wiped out. Currently, Qianjiang is garrisoned by a regiment, a security team with four detachments, totaling 446 men. The militia organization in the city and countryside is tightly organized, with a total of five districts divided into 159 brigades, 636 companies, and 1,908 squads, totaling 68,688 people. They are in close contact with each other, establishing peasant outposts and relaying urgent reports, so that news spreads quickly in the event of a bandit alarm, and they defend together. After Qianjiang was ravaged by the bandits, nine out of ten houses were empty. The people lacked food and could only eat water chestnuts, and they could not even eat their fill each day. The fields were barren, and the farmers lacked both seeds and cattle. They often had to pull iron plows with several people to work the land. After the recovery, there was no harvest in the winter, and relief was urgently needed. The Department of Civil Affairs had previously allocated 25,000 yuan, but it was a drop in the bucket and did not solve the problem. The land had been disposed of by the bandits, and the land deeds were burned. It is now being handled in accordance with the regulations for the handling of rural land in the Communist suppression area issued by the headquarters, and the results are good. As for education, there were several primary schools, but they were completely suspended after the bandit disaster and cannot be established now. There are only two private schools in the city to educate children. There is a Catholic parish in the city, presided over by Father Luo Degong. The Catholic Church originally established primary schools for boys and girls in the city, but they have not been restored since the bandit disaster. There is only a private school-style primary school. When the reporter arrived in Qianjiang at 11 AM on the 9th, the villages seen along the way were dilapidated. After entering the city, although the shops had opened, there was nothing to buy except snacks. After a short rest at the county government, I went to the parade ground to observe the militia and then inspected Shenhuotan, the site of fierce battles between the National Army and the bandits. Although the traces of the battle are no longer discernible, the remnants of the bandit's pseudo-Hunan-Hubei-West Provincial Soviet Presidium Finance Department bulletin and the Red Army soldiers and various slogans of the pseudo-Workers' and Peasants' Red Army Third Army Ninth Division remain. The bulletin of the pseudo-Finance Department, which was posted when the officers and soldiers were suppressing bandits, shows their general situation of draining the pond to catch all the fish and economic panic. Excerpts are as follows for reference: "(1) Land tax is determined according to the value of agricultural products. No tax is levied for values less than 50 yuan. From 50 yuan to 100 yuan, 1% is levied (i.e., one cent per yuan; the following applies similarly). From 100 yuan to 200 yuan, 2% is levied. From 200 yuan to 300 yuan, 3% is levied. From 300 yuan to 500 yuan, 5% is levied. From 500 yuan to 700 yuan, 7% is levied. From 700 yuan to 1,000 yuan, 10% is levied. (2) Wealthy farmers in the past are taxed double according to one standard. (3) Workers themselves are exempt from tax, but their families, parents, wives, and children are still taxed according to their harvest. (4) Red Army family members are taxed at half the rate. The families of Red soldiers who sacrificed in the revolutionary war are exempt from tax altogether. (5) (Original text incomplete) tax-exempt, but due to the current economic difficulties, it is decided to borrow half according to the standard of the Spring Committee land tax, and the borrowed funds will be repaid when taxes are collected in the autumn. (6) Taxes can be paid in both money and grain. (7) Soviet water conservancy bonds and bank banknotes must be repaid when taxes are collected in the autumn." (Issued in Yuekou on December 9)

Zhu Zhaoxin Dies in Guangzhou 106

Doctor's Examination Suspects Cerebral Hemorrhage

Guangdong Government Sends Personnel to Handle Funeral and Discuss Compensation

Guangzhou Correspondence: Zhu Zhaoxin, Diplomatic Inspector of the Five Southwest Provinces and Member of the Guangdong Provincial Government, suddenly died at home on the night of the 10th of this month after attending a naval banquet. Zhu was in good health in Japan as usual. After working, he went to dinner at the home of his friend Pan. The dinner was a snake soup feast. After the banquet, he accepted an invitation from the Navy Headquarters to attend a banquet hosted by the Guangdong Navy for British Admiral Cary. In addition to Navy Commander Zhang Zhiying, Chen Jitang, Liu Jiwen, and others were present that evening. Zhu was in high spirits and drank heartily until the banquet ended. He returned home in a drunken state. On the way, in the carriage, he suddenly felt unwell. When he arrived at his private residence on Ruixing New Street, he felt a severe headache. His family thought Zhu was drunk and gave him hangover medicine, but it was ineffective. After taking a headache remedy, he felt slightly better and rested for about half an hour. The headache became more severe, and he vomited and had diarrhea. His moans indicated he was in critical condition. The whole family was at a loss. When Chinese and Western doctors arrived, Zhu's heart had already stopped. The doctors were helpless. At approximately 2:10 AM on the morning of the 11th, Zhu's family, fearing that his sudden death was due to other causes, summoned Dr. Huang to examine the remains. It was determined that the corpse's joints were stiff and the fingernails were blue, which are inevitable conditions after death and cannot prove the cause of death. There were no other abnormalities. Considering his general symptoms after a full meal and heavy drinking, and at his age and physical condition, cerebral hemorrhage (commonly known as stroke) was the most likely cause. After Zhu's death, his family arranged for the funeral. The Provincial Government also sent personnel to assist. A coffin worth a thousand yuan has already been purchased, and the encoffining ceremony is scheduled for this morning (the 13th). It is reported that the Provincial Government will submit a proposal to the Provincial Council on the 14th to discuss generous compensation. Zhu is survived by five sons and seven daughters.

The eldest son graduated in England and returned to Guangdong and is already self-reliant. His mother is over seventy years old and still in good health. Zhu was frugal and left behind a modest estate. (December 13)

Wuxi

Seven Bandits Rob in a Car 108

Zhu Yunsheng, a resident of Zhu Xie Lane, Kaiyuan Township, Fourth District, Wuxi County, runs an iron shop in Shanghai and is wealthy. Only his wife, children, and servants live at home. Unexpectedly, seven bandits suddenly arrived in a car the other night from the city. Four of them wore overcoats, and three wore plain clothes. They were armed with pistols, flashlights, and other weapons. They broke into the house and ordered everyone to be silent. They ransacked the house and looted two gold Buddhas, two gold ingots, and jewelry, totaling over 2,000 yuan. They abandoned the bulky clothing and did not take it. After looting, the bandits sped away in the original car towards the city. Afterwards, Zhu's wife informed Zhu Yunsheng in Shanghai by long-distance telephone and reported the matter to the County Bureau for investigation.

Dispute Over Closure of Hefeng Silk Factory 109

Taifeng Silk Factory, located in Longchuanbang outside the West Gate of Wuxi, was established by Zhang Zizhen and others. This year, it was renamed Hefeng, and Zhang Zizhen became the sole proprietor and manager. Since its opening, it has never stopped operating, and business has been doing well. On the 10th of this month, the factory summoned all the foremen and indicated that it would have to stop work for three days starting on the 15th. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 15th, the factory's accountant, Zhang Zhonghou, suddenly summoned all the foremen and said that the factory was affected by the low price of silk and the lack of raw materials and had decided to temporarily close down. All employees will also be temporarily dismissed, and meals for the foremen will be provided until the 20th. Salaries will be paid until the end of the month. Upon hearing the news, the employees believed that according to the old custom, the salary for the twelfth lunar month must be doubled. Now that the factory suddenly stopped work, not only was the doubled salary hopeless, but their livelihood would also be cut off. They immediately elected representatives to request the factory three times to provide meals until the end of the year and pay salaries until March, in accordance with the company's regulations for the closure and dismissal of employees, in order to maintain the livelihood of the employees. As manager Zhang Zizhen was ill at home, Zhang Zhonghou represented him and stated that the factory was in financial difficulty and could not accept the request. The employees, driven by livelihood, had no choice but to struggle desperately. Therefore, they decided to directly request Zhang Zizhen again today and temporarily withhold the wages paid to the female workers to help supplement the funds.

County Chamber of Commerce Requests Allotment of抵借券 110

The provincial government issued抵借券(Offset Bond), and the County Chamber of Commerce was allotted 22,000 yuan of the 69,000 yuan quota in this county, which should be raised by various industries. The Chamber of Commerce convened representatives from various industries yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. More than 30 representatives from various industries attended. Chairman Qian Sunqing reported the purpose of the meeting, and then the representatives from various industries expressed their opinions, stating that at this time of year, business was sluggish and they were unable to undertake the task. It was decided by the public that the Chamber of Commerce should state the plight of various industries and request the county government to forward the matter to the provincial government for approval.

Zhenjiang

Liu Youyu Abruptly Closes Due to Deficit 111

Liu Youyu Ham Shop, which has been open for decades, is one of the best in the province. In the past, it specialized in selling to Hong Kong, Southeast Asia, and other places, and business was very prosperous. In recent years, because the hams shipped to Hong Kong were deemed unsanitary and purchased from Suzhou and Hangzhou instead, sales have declined, and it has only relied on scattered wholesale and retail sales to eke out a living. The profits of the past have been exhausted, and recently it has become more and more difficult to make ends meet. Yesterday, it declared bankruptcy. It owes 4,060 taels of silver to Yuanyi Village, 1,167 taels of silver to each of Jinsheng and Tongyu, 700 taels of silver to Jishanji, about 2,000 taels of silver and 2,100 yuan of foreign currency to depositors, and over 300 taels of silver and over 1,900 yuan of foreign currency to Shanghai for goods. The total is about 19,000 yuan of foreign currency. After deducting the inventories, accounts receivable, and assets as collateral, the net loss is over 13,000 yuan.

Changzhou

Rickshaw Puller Suspected in Robbery on Return Trip 112

Yu Wang, a widow from Xiatang, Qishuyan, in Wu County, is related to Sun Jinsheng, a partner at Tianyitai Foreign Goods Store in the city. Yu Wang came to the city on the 14th to visit her relatives and hired a rickshaw in the evening to go to the station and return home. When she arrived at Wangsun Lane on the east side of the Confucian Temple, a Sichuanese bandit suddenly pressed the rickshaw down and robbed Yu Wang of the rattan bag, scarf, and other items she was carrying. At the time, the rickshaw puller did not resist at all, as if he had a tacit agreement with the bandits. After the robbery, he still forced Yu Wang to go to the station. Yu Wang cried and begged to return to her relative's house. The rickshaw returned to the Tianyitai Foreign Goods Store, where the store captured the rickshaw puller, Yi Jinbao, and sent him to the First Public Security Bureau. Yi confessed that the robber was Yang Yuqiao. On the morning of the 15th, Yang and related person Zhu Liuguanzi were captured and escorted to the county government for interrogation.

The Jiangbei long-distance bus, which departed from Gaoyou for Qingjiang the day before, overturned into the canal at Mapengwan due to excessive speed. After people tried their best to rescue it, one passenger drowned, and the other six passengers and the driver were injured. There is no danger to their lives.

They immediately tied up Cao's elderly mother in her sixties with rope and beat her into injury. Then they crowded into the bedroom and searched extensively, stealing silver coins, clothes, and other items worth about 300 yuan.

Huang Boqiao Appointed Director of the Two Railways Administration 121

He Arrived at the Bureau Yesterday Afternoon to Take Over

Announcing the Appointments of Mo Heng and Yuan Boyang

As Chief and Deputy Chief of the General Affairs Department

After the January 28th Shanghai Incident this spring, the ineffectiveness of the responsible person at the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration led the Ministry of Railways to promote the commissioner of the bureau, Chen Xinghan, to the position of director. At that time, the traffic on the two railways was crucial for the deployment of our anti-Japanese troops and the relief of war-zone victims. Although Mr. Chen took office during this difficult time, he was able to fulfill his duties by working hard and giving directions. However, due to a lack of construction skills, there were high expectations and strict demands from all sides for the reconstruction of the two railways. Therefore, there was a growing dissatisfaction with Mr. Chen. As a result, Mr. Chen had no choice but to submit his resignation to the Ministry, which was approved yesterday by the Ministry of Railways. The current Director of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, Huang Boqiao, was appointed to succeed him. The details are as follows:

Director of the Two Railways Administration, Mr. Huang Boqiao

(Chen's Resignation Approved) The Ministry of Railways received Mr. Chen's resignation and decided to approve it. However, there was no suitable candidate for the successor. After deliberation, it was decided to transfer the current Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, Mr. Huang Boqiao, to succeed him. The Minister Huang then sent someone to Shanghai to solicit his opinion. Mr. Huang replied that he had served in Shanghai for a long time, and various construction projects were just beginning to take shape. If Mayor Wu did not agree, he would not be willing to leave his original post. Upon receiving the report, Minister Gu took advantage of Mayor Wu's trip to Beijing to attend the Third Plenary Session of the Central Committee to solicit his opinion in person. It was then decided to jointly send a telegram to Shanghai summoning Mr. Huang to Beijing.

(Mr. Huang Goes to Beijing) After receiving the telegram, Mr. Huang went to Beijing on the 14th to meet with Minister Gu and Mayor Wu. Minister Gu stated that Director Huang was known for his capable handling of affairs and was praised by all parties. Moreover, the reconstruction of the two railways and the construction of the new station were not only major responsibilities but also had a significant relationship with the implementation of the Greater Shanghai Plan. Mayor Wu immediately expressed his approval, and Mr. Huang also agreed. The Ministry of Railways also added a deputy director position due to the complexity and importance of the two railways affairs, appointing Wu Shaozeng to the post. After receiving the order, Mr. Huang returned to Shanghai yesterday morning, first going to the Public Utilities Bureau to make arrangements for the handover.

(Arrived at the Bureau Yesterday Afternoon) At 3 p.m., the two directors, Huang and Wu, along with Mo Heng, the former chief of the Fourth Section of the Public Utilities Bureau, and Yuan Boyang, the chief of the First Section, went to the Two Railways Administration to take over. Chen Xinghan first gathered all the staff to introduce the new directors and delivered a speech. After the meeting, former Director Chen assigned the Chief of the General Affairs Department, Kaihua, to handle the handover, clarifying all the files and documents of the General Affairs Department. The new director then announced the appointments of Mo Heng as the Chief of the General Affairs Department and Yuan Boyang as the Deputy Chief. The remaining staff were not changed. After completing the handover, Director Huang left the bureau at around 5 p.m. and returned to his residence.

(Key Points of the Speech) After arriving at the bureau, Director Huang delivered a speech to all the staff, briefly stating that although he had firmly declined, Minister Gu had entrusted him with the position of Director of the bureau, which was not approved. He was here today to take office and would work hard to serve and live up to the expectations of the people and Minister Gu. There were four key points: 1. The advancement and demotion of the bureau's staff would be based entirely on their performance, so please work with peace of mind. 2. The establishment of railway facilities should be based on public opinion. 3. The transportation of the railway should strive to increase efficiency to the highest possible degree. 4. The construction of the new station should be carried out in cooperation with the Shanghai Municipal Government, so that it can be completed as soon as possible.

(Background of Huang and Wu) Huang Boqiao is 43 years old, a native of Taicang County, Jiangsu Province, and a graduate of the first class of the Mechanical Engineering Department of Tongji Medical and Engineering University in Shanghai. He studied at the Berlin University of Technology in Germany and served as the chief of the General Affairs Section of the Road Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications in Beijing, a member of the Railway Dictionary Revision Committee of the Ministry of Communications, the chief of the General Affairs Department of the Bian-Luo Road of the Longhai Railway, the director of the Public Works Bureau of Hankou City, the director of the Public Works Bureau of Hangzhou City, the director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, the secretary-general of the Shanghai Municipal Government, the chairman of the Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Engineering Society, and a director of the Chinese Institute of Engineers. He represented the Beijing, Shanghai, and Hankou municipal governments, the Construction Committee, and the Chinese Engineering Society at the Second World Power Conference held in Berlin, Germany. Deputy Director Wu Shaozeng is a commissioner of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways and is experienced in railway construction and transportation. He has been instrumental in the implementation of responsible transportation on various railways recently.
