The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Supports Increasing the Bond Fund 123

Key Points of Mr. Zhou's Proposal

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram yesterday supporting the proposal to increase the bond fund. The original text of the telegram reads: "To the Third Plenary Session of the Central Committee in Nanjing, we are delighted to read that Committee Member Zhou Fohai and others have proposed to increase the bond fund and repay the principal in advance. The reduction of interest rates and the extension of the term of bonds were originally intended to help the government overcome difficulties during the national crisis by bondholders. However, since its implementation, bond prices have fallen, the financial market has been affected, and the commercial economy has been hindered. Now that the Plenary Session has opened, the government is making efforts to build a new vision, and the restoration of social finance must be the first step. Only then will there be a way to utilize private capital. We respectfully request that the Plenary Session pass the aforementioned proposal and hand it over to the National Government for prompt implementation, so as to show the people the way to trust them while taking into account both the national economy and the people's livelihood. We cannot help but anxiously hope for this in our telegram, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

Xin Sheng News Agency reported that Mr. Zhou Fohai, the original proposer, said that the key points of the proposal were as follows: "Since the establishment of the country, a large amount of public debt and treasury bonds has been issued. The people's support for the government is undeniable. The fund used by the government to guarantee the repayment of principal and interest is also reliable, which enables it to repay principal and interest on time and maintain stable credit. Therefore, the bond price has often been around 70% to 80% of its face value. However, since the Liaoning Incident, bond prices have plummeted, and the market has been shaken. Both finance and economy have suffered. After the Shanghai Incident, financial stagnation and social exhaustion occurred, and the bond market fell to a new low. Fortunately, the bondholders understood the situation and negotiated with the government to reduce the interest rate of various public debt and treasury bonds and extend the repayment period in order to slightly reduce the financial pressure of the government and maintain bond credit. The people's solidarity with the country is commendable. However, for the government, this is ultimately an expedient measure and cannot be regarded as a permanent rule. Moreover, the people's concept of credit for national public debt has not been restored. This can be seen from the fact that the circulation price of bonds has not recovered to its old value in recent months. If people do not develop a deep sense of trust in the country and the government, then at a time when this new country is being built, post-disaster relief in the communist areas, reconstruction of the war zones, and countless problems all require funds. What can the government rely on to regulate these funds? For the sake of cultivating the people's trust in the country and for the sake of the government's future construction, a more favorable method should be adopted for the repayment of principal and interest of the public debt and treasury bonds that have been issued. According to the case of revising the schedule of repayment of principal and interest of public debt and treasury bonds in January of this year, although the National Government has clearly ordered it to be finalized and not to be changed again, the so-called no more changes refers to the fact that the fund must not be shaken in the slightest. If the government increases the fund outside the original fund and repays the principal in advance, it will not conflict with the original plan. It is specially proposed that the National Government of our country should take advantage of this opportunity to move back to the capital and start anew with the people. As the political situation is gradually stabilizing and tax revenue is gradually improving, the government should automatically increase the monthly allocation of the bond principal and interest fund from January of the 21st year of the Republic of China by three to four million yuan on top of the original allocation of half of the fund of 8.6 million yuan. For bond repayment, the method specified when the bonds were issued should be fully restored, and the term should no longer be extended. While it may seem that the government is allocating more funds and the finances may be affected, the organs may need to be streamlined, the financial market will benefit greatly from the people's perspective, and the concept of the government's maintenance of debt credit will be more firmly established as a result. The willingness to cooperate with the government will also be more practical as a result."

Eurasia Aviation Corporation

General Manager Li Takes Office 124

Discusses the Importance of Opening the Northwest Route

Returned to Beijing Last Night to Report Details

The Ri Ri News Agency reported that the board of directors of Eurasia Aviation Corporation appointed Li Jingcong, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Communications, as the general manager of the company on the 14th of this month. Li took office at the company at 9 a.m. yesterday and telegraphed the Ministry of Communications and notified all stations. A Ri Ri News Agency reporter visited Li yesterday morning, who gave a detailed account of the reasons for the reorganization and the difficulties and importance of opening the Northwest Route. The following is a record of Li's remarks:

(Reasons for Reorganization) "I (Li referred to himself) originally served as the Director of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Communications, and my affairs were very busy. I was unable to take care of the company's affairs. However, the former General Manager Wang Zhiyuan was unable to serve concurrently due to the heavy responsibilities of the Northeast National Salvation Army. He earnestly resigned, and Minister Zhu Jiahua had no choice but to have me take over. I took over today (yesterday). The Eurasia Northwest Route is not only closely related to the development of the Northwest but also has great value internationally. I deeply hope that all sectors will provide assistance so that it can continue to develop."

(Difficulties in Opening the Route) "The Eurasia Northwest Route was originally scheduled to officially open on the 15th, but the opening was postponed by one day due to a slight obstruction of the aircraft's parts during takeoff. It officially opened today (yesterday). However, although it has now opened, there are still many difficulties. The more important ones are listed as follows: 1. Regarding aircraft parts, the company's aircraft parts were not very numerous to begin with. In addition, there have been damages in recent months, and the remaining parts are extremely limited. For this route, which makes round trips of approximately 10,000 kilometers per week, even if there are no obstacles along the way, the allocation is difficult, and new aircraft parts cannot be delivered until February of next year at the earliest. This is the first difficulty. 2. Regarding ground equipment, the climate in the Northwest is severely cold, and it is already cool in October. In this environment, it is difficult to fly on schedule without sheds, houses, and heating equipment. These have not been considered in the past few months, and it is impossible to build them now. Other equipment such as wireless weather instruments are also very important for flight, but they have not been prepared, and there is no way to purchase them locally because the supply is not meeting demand. They can only be gradually transported and arranged. This is the second difficulty. 3. Regarding personnel, the company specializes in air transportation and is jointly operated by China and Germany. All German technicians have been in China for less than two years and cannot be expected to be fluent in Chinese. Therefore, in order to ensure smooth operation and convenient management, senior Chinese officials should be those who have aviation and business knowledge and are also fluent in German. It is already not easy to find such people, and the general mentality of the Chinese people is that they view the Northwest as a long distance.

Page 12

Most people are afraid to go. In fact, the resources in the Northwest are far richer than those in the inland provinces, and the climate is drier than that in the Jiangnan area. Moreover, the company is developing air transportation, and although the Northwest is tens of thousands of miles away, the round-trip flight in the future will only take three to four days. However, even after explaining this to these talents, they still have difficulties. This is another difficulty. As for the storage and transportation of gasoline and the construction of airports along the way, I ordered the company to handle them separately or entrusted them to local officials when I test-flew to Xinjiang last year, so they are no longer a problem. In short, no matter how difficult it is, I will try to make it perfect in the shortest possible time, so as to live up to the expectations of Minister Zhu and the people of the society."

(Importance of Opening the Route) "After the entire Northwest Route is completed, all mail to Europe can be transported by the company's aircraft to Tacheng on the Sino-Russian border and transferred to the Siberian Railway, arriving in Europe in 13 to 14 days. Now that China and Russia have restored diplomatic relations, it is easier to proceed with the method of flying directly to Europe. In the future, Eurasia airmail will only take five to six days to transport, and the government's original goal of blocking Northeast postal services can also be completely achieved. Once all facilities are in place, I plan to fly to Russia in person to discuss with the Russian authorities the specific methods for the company's aircraft to transport mail through Russian territory and fly to Europe, or to temporarily use aircraft for intermodal transport on the Sino-Russian border, etc."

(Telegraph to the Ministry of Communications) After taking office yesterday, Li telegraphed the Ministry of Communications separately and notified all aircraft stations. The original text is extracted below: 1. "Respectfully submit that the board of directors of Eurasia Aviation Corporation has decided to appoint Jingcong as the vice chairman of Eurasia Aviation Corporation and to appoint him as the general manager by the chairman of the board. With this approval, Jingcong took office at the company on December 16th and is reporting to the Ministry for review and filing. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Communications. 2. "To Minister Zhu and Vice Minister Yu Zhang of the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing, Jingcong has been appointed by the board of directors of Eurasia Aviation Corporation as the vice chairman and general manager of the company. He will take office at the company today. This is hereby reported by telegram. Li Jingcong, General Manager of Eurasia Aviation Corporation."

(Notice to All Stations) "To the stationmaster, the board of directors of Eurasia Aviation Corporation has decided to appoint Jingcong as the vice chairman of Eurasia Aviation Corporation and to appoint him as the general manager by the chairman of the board. With this approval, Jingcong took office at the company on December 16th. In addition to reporting to the Ministry of Communications and sending separate letters, this letter is hereby sent for your information."

(Returned to Beijing Last Night) After Li took office at the company yesterday morning, he reported the official opening of the Northwest Route to Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua and took the night express train to Beijing at 11:45 last night to report everything in person and handle official business in the ministry. It is said that Li will return to Shanghai in three or four days.

Local Chinese Merchants Prepare to Order Russian Goods 126

The Consulate to Resume After the Announcement of the Personnel Selection The Central News Agency reported that, according to diplomatic sources, after the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, all existing treaties between China and Russia will continue to be valid until a new treaty is signed. The Central News Agency reporter, in view of the importance of the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, explored and recorded various situations regarding the relationship between China and Russia as follows:

Compilation of Sino-Russian Treaties 127

1. The first treaty signed between China and Russia was the Sino-Russian Treaty signed on the 3rd day of the 5th month of the 8th year of Xianfeng in the Qing Dynasty, with a total of 12 articles. The main points of the treaty were to allow Russia to trade in seven seaports, including Shanghai, Ningbo, Fuzhou, Xiamen, Guangzhou, Taiwan, and Qiongzhou. 2. The Sino-Russian Supplementary Treaty of the 10th year of Xianfeng, with a total of 15 articles, focused on borders and trade. 3. The revised Sino-Russian Land Trade Regulations of the 8th year of Tongzhi, with a total of 22 articles, focused on tariffs. 4. The revised Sino-Russian Treaty of the 7th year of Guangxu, with a total of 20 articles, mainly focused on compensating Russian soldiers for guarding Ili and compensating Russian citizens for various cases. 5. The revised Sino-Russian Land Trade Regulations of the same year, with a total of 17 articles, revised tariffs. 6. The Sino-Russian Treaty of the 24th year of Guangxu, with a total of 9 articles, leased Lushun and Dalian Bay. 7. The Sino-Russian Supplementary Treaty of the same year, with a total of 6 articles, mainly focused on borders. 8. The Sino-Russian Special Treaty for the Demarcation of the Lushun and Dalian Bay Lease Areas of the 25th year of Guangxu, with a total of 8 articles, demarcated borders. 9. The Sino-Russian Treaty on the Handover of the Three Eastern Provinces of the 28th year of Guangxu, with a total of 4 articles, concerned the borders and railways of the Three Eastern Provinces. 10. The Sino-Russian Treaty on the Return of the Railways Outside the Pass of the same year, with a total of 7 articles, concerned postal and telecommunications and the stationing of troops outside the Pass. 11. The Outline Clauses for the Establishment of Public Councils in the Railway Zone of the Sino-Russian Eastern Province of the 1st year of Xuantong, with a total of 18 articles and 2 attachments, stipulated the treatment of Chinese and foreign people in the railway zone. 12. The Sino-Mongolian Agreement of the 1st year of the Republic of China, with a total of 4 articles. 13. The Sino-Russian Treaty on the Treatment of Outer Mongolia of the 2nd year of the Republic of China, with a total of 5 articles and 3 declarations. 14. The Sino-Mongolian Bank Agreement of the 4th year of the Republic of China, with a total of 5 main points. 15. The Sino-Russian Hulunbuir Treaty of the 4th year of the Republic of China, with a total of 3 main points. 16. The Annex to the Continued Payment of the Boxer Indemnity to Russia of the 7th year of the Republic of China, with a total of 3 main points. 17. The Sino-Russian Provisional Trade Treaty of Ili of the 9th year of the Republic of China, with a total of 11 articles. 18. The Sino-Russian Preliminary Trade Treaty of the 11th year of the Republic of China, with a total of 5 articles. 19. The Outline Agreement for the Settlement of Outstanding Sino-Russian Issues of the 13th year of the Republic of China, with a total of 15 articles, including: (A) Prohibition of each other from propaganda contrary to the public order and social organization of the other country; (B) The Soviet Russian government agreed to waive part of Russia's share of the Boxer Indemnity; (C) The Soviet Russian government agreed to abolish extraterritoriality and consular jurisdiction. 20. The Provisional Agreement on the Management of the Chinese Eastern Railway of the 13th year of the Republic of China, with a total of 10 articles and 7 declarations.

Current Situation of Russian Goods in China 128

There are almost no overall statistics on the trade of Russian goods in China. According to Russian merchants, after the severance of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, maritime transportation was suspended, and transportation relied on foreign mail ships, with high freight rates. Therefore, the trade in China has declined year by year in the past five years. The main goods transported to China are kerosene and cloth, but due to the reliance on foreign transportation, it is difficult to compete with other countries. Now that diplomatic relations have been restored and sea routes have been opened, Russian goods will definitely be able to seize the labor of Japanese goods in China.

Shanghai Merchants Plan to Order Russian Goods 129

Russia's industrial and commercial development surpasses that of any other country. Moreover, its goods are abundant, leading to low prices, even lower than those of Japanese goods, which are known for their cheapness. Now that China and Russia have resumed diplomatic relations, Russian merchants are planning to restore shipping services to facilitate transportation. Since the movement to boycott foreign goods, local Shanghai merchants have been actively promoting domestic products. To replace the goods that domestic production lacks, they are now planning to order Russian goods. It is said that some local merchants have already begun negotiating with Russian merchants to place orders.

Restoration of Consulate Awaits 130

Since the severance of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, Russian expatriates in China have been managed by German consulates on behalf of the Soviet Russian government. However, according to information from the German consulate, they were never entrusted by the Soviet Russian government to manage Russian expatriates in Shanghai. They were only entrusted to manage the Russian Consulate General building at No. 1 on the Bund. Furthermore, that building was returned to the Russian side for self-management last year. Therefore, the restoration of the Russian Consulate General will likely occur after the appointment of consular personnel.

Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bonds

Issuance Commenced Yesterday 131

To rescue the silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the Ministry of Finance issued public bonds totaling 3 million yuan. The regulations and subsidy measures have been announced. These public bonds are now held by the Fund Custody Committee. Any stored silk from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces that has been registered and qualified for export by the organization committee can, starting yesterday, be presented to the Promotion Committee along with the stored silk export permit and public quantity sheet to obtain a registration certificate. Northern Wharf of China Merchants Bureau Not Interrupted 133

Talk by Liu Hongsheng

According to the Central News Agency, Liu Hongsheng, General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau, told a Central News Agency reporter yesterday that reports stating that workers at the Northern Wharf had resumed work today (i.e., yesterday) were completely untrue. There had never been a strike by workers at the Northern Wharf. Although the workers from the five wharves had petitioned the Bureau to withdraw the order due to the He (Tiehua) issue, after explanation, they understood and returned to work. He Tiehua has also resumed his duties, and all employees are working as usual without interruption. According to reports yesterday, the wharf handled over 150 pieces of cargo. This proves that the strike rumors are completely false. The current unrest is likely due to a few employees who feared being laid off and incited others. The Bureau does not attach much importance to this. Regarding the Chinese wharves, the monthly salary for staff at this wharf was 798 yuan in the same month of the 17th year of the Republic. This month, it has gradually increased to 2,570 yuan, more than tripling in four years. However, the income in the last two years is only 4,300 taels, and the official interest and depreciation of assets are not included. If calculated in silver dollars, 4,000 taels is approximately 6,000 yuan, which is only enough to pay salaries for six months. This phenomenon is astonishing. The past corruption of the China Merchants Bureau can be seen from this. Regarding the overall reorganization plan, although it cannot be drafted in a short time, the accumulated problems in various parts must be rectified at any time.

Public Prosecution by Local Court Against Chen and Li in Original Text 134

The embezzlement and loan case of the China Merchants Bureau has been publicly prosecuted by the Local Court Prosecutors Ouyang Shu and Xie Lian. The original text of the indictment is recorded below:

Defendant Chen Fumu, male, age unknown, from Guangdong, whereabouts unknown, former Deputy Minister of Transportation and Supervisor of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau; Li Guojie, male, 52 years old, from Hefei, Anhui, resident at 1050 Avenue Joffre, former General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau. The aforementioned defendants are accused of dereliction of duty and breach of trust in Case No. 4671 (Xin Zi) of the 21st year of the Republic of China. The investigation has been completed according to law and the prosecution believes that the case warrants public prosecution. The facts of the defendants' crimes and the applicable legal provisions are listed below:

Defendant Chen Fumu, while serving as Deputy Minister of Transportation and Supervisor of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau, and Defendant Li Guojie, while serving as Chairman and General Manager, with the Bureau being privately owned but state-operated, allegedly used the name of revitalizing the business to mortgage and lease the Bureau's real estate and docks located in Shanghai to the American China Business Corporation on September 5th and 6th of this year, at an interest rate of nine percent per month, borrowing 20 million Shanghai taels of silver (after deducting 15% discount and 2.5% commission, each 10 million taels was only 8.25 million). They also signed a three-wharf lease and a memorandum for the purchase of ships on credit, resulting in significant losses of shipping rights and assets. After signing, they submitted the documents to the Supervisory Office for stamping. Chen Fumu took the opportunity to solicit bribes and withheld the documents, neither issuing them nor submitting them to the Ministry for approval. Li Guojie then negotiated with the China Business Corporation to advance 700,000 taels of silver, sending Bao Yaoting to the China Merchants Bureau office at 3 PM on September 23rd of the same year, to deliver the funds to Li Guojie. Li Guojie issued a receipt with the Bureau's seal and handed it to Huang Jusu, Chen Fumu's representative, who then returned the stamped contracts and other documents to Li Guojie, who passed them on to Bao Yaoting. Li Guojie confessed to the Ministry of Transportation on December 13th of this year, and the investigation confirmed the facts. The aforementioned facts are based on the following evidence: (1) Loan contracts, mortgage deeds, leases, and memoranda; (2) China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau receipt for 700,000 taels advanced by the China Business Corporation; (3) Confession of Li Guojie; (4) Statement of Bao Yaoting that at 3-4 PM on September 23rd of this year, the General Manager of the American China Business Corporation told me to deliver 700,000 taels to the China Merchants Bureau, including 150,000 taels converted into silver dollars, personally handed them to Li Guojie, obtained a receipt, and Li Guojie gave me a large package of contracts to take back to the company, which matches Li Guojie's account of the amounts of silver and silver dollars and the simultaneous exchange of contracts; (5) Testimony of Qu Shuyou and Yao Dekui stating that No. 28 Meiliyuan is Chen Fumu's family residence, with no one else living there. He has a wife and children, but we don't know their names; Investigation of Jin Cheng, Shanghai Zhong Fu, and San Xing Bank accounts shows that on September 24th and 26th of this year, new accounts were opened under the names of Chen Zesheng, Chen Shaode, and Ms. Wei Houming, depositing a total of 200,000 taels of silver, which were part of the 700,000 taels advanced by the American China Business Corporation to Li Guojie. The addresses of the account holders are all No. 28 Meiliyuan on Daxilu. Since that address is Chen Fumu's family residence, Chen Zesheng and others are undoubtedly aliases of Chen Fumu; (6) Of the 700,000 taels of silver advanced by the American China Business Corporation to Li Guojie, in addition to the aforementioned 200,000 taels transferred through the Postal Savings Bureau and the four-bank reserve, the remaining 400,000 taels were deposited in the names of Huang Zhengde at the Shanghai Bank (100,000 taels), Huang Weiru at the Jing'an Temple branch of the Shanghai Bank (100,000 taels), Feng Duanyi at the Shanghai Bank (50,000 taels), Huang Dade at the Hongkou branch of the Bank of China (50,000 taels), Feng Shuyan at the Bank of China (50,000 taels), and Huang Zhongde at the Zhong Fu Bank (50,000 taels) (all confirmed by official inquiries). After summoning the account holders Huang Zhengde and others to their registered addresses, none of them were found, indicating that they are all aliases of Chen Fumu. In summary, the defendants Chen Fumu and Li Guojie, as public officials, had the responsibility to manage and operate the China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau. They regrettably signed contracts that harmed shipping rights and damaged the Bureau's assets, clearly constituting dereliction of duty and breach of trust, unlawfully causing damage to the China Merchants Bureau, jointly violating Article 366, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, and should be punished according to Articles 140 and 42 of the same law. Chen Fumu accepted bribes and failed to submit the signed contracts to the Ministry for approval, clearly violating his duties, violating Article 129, Paragraph 2 of the same law, and should be punished according to Paragraph 4 of the same article and Article 70 of the same law. Li Guojie, for paying bribes to a public official who violated his duties, also violated Paragraph 3 of the same article, and confessed his crime, so he should also be punished according to Articles 74, 70, and 38, Paragraph 1 of the same law. Therefore, in accordance with Article 253, Paragraphs 1 and 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law, prosecution is initiated and the case is submitted for trial. To the Criminal Division of this Court. Prosecutors Ouyang Shu and Xie Lian, December 10, 21st year of the Republic of China. This is a true copy, certified to be identical to the original. Clerk Wang Shanxiang.

Completion of Two New Naval Vessels, Trial Run in Longhua Yesterday 135

Flag-Raising Ceremony on New Year's Day

The Navy Department's newly constructed Jiangning and Haining vessels, launched after the Mid-Autumn Festival, have progressed rapidly. Construction is now complete. The Haining vessel had a trial run once before. The Jiangning vessel, led by Inspector Guo Chen, also conducted a trial run yesterday morning from 8:00 AM to Longhua Bay, returning after 12:00 PM with excellent results. The tonnage and artillery of the two vessels are the same, with a displacement of 280 tons, a length of 180 feet, a width of 20 feet, a draft of 6 feet, and a speed of 12 nautical miles per hour. The vessels are equipped with two 5.7-inch guns at the front and rear, and three machine guns. The aforementioned guns can also be used as anti-aircraft guns. It is currently scheduled to sail out of the Wusong Estuary to the Sanjia Water Sea on the 25th for gunnery trials. A flag-raising and formation ceremony will be held on New Year's Day next year. Jiangning vessel Captain Jiang Hengshi, formerly Captain of the Rensheng vessel, has been appointed by the Navy Department to take command. The entire vessel's complement includes one first lieutenant captain, one second lieutenant first officer, one second lieutenant engineering officer, and soldiers.

Resumption of Production at Double Palace Silk Factories 139

Furlon Factory Starts Work, Hong Lun Factory Prepares

India Sales Improve, Inventory Decreases

Of the original seven double palace silk factories in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, including Furlon in Shanghai, all but Furlon and Hong Lun had been forced to suspend operations successively due to the severe decline in the European and American double palace silk market. In October of this year, due to the complete lack of transactions in the European and American double palace silk market, exports of double palace silk disappeared and inventory piled up. To avoid significant losses, operations were temporarily suspended to await an opportunity. Recently, although the European and American double palace silk market remains unattended, sales in India are still strong. To maintain the livelihoods of workers, the Furlon factory at the end of Tianbao Road, with 216 machines and about 380 female workers, managed by Shen Zupei, resumed operations yesterday. As for the Hong Lun factory on Liuying Road, with 204 machines and about 350 female workers, managed by Fei Yangzhi, it has already organized its machinery and is preparing to resume operations the day after tomorrow.

The Tragic Plight of a Ten-Year-Old Girl

Only Two Meals a Day 143

Beaten While Moping

The Lin Couple with Bad Hearts

Luckily the Benevolent Child Rescue Society Reports

Wang Azhen Finally Escapes from the Pit

The China Benevolent Relief Society at No. 20 Museum Road, founded by former Minister of Industry and Commerce Kong Xiangxi, and the Benevolent Child Education Institute, founded by Mrs. Kong at No. 93 Huishan Road, are dedicated to rescuing and educating impoverished children without resources, so that they can increase their knowledge and avoid falling into crime in the future. The morning before yesterday, the Relief Society received a phone report stating that a girl at No. 714 Meifuli, Parker Road, was being cruelly treated by her master and was suffering terribly. The Relief Society sent representatives Zhang Yueru and Ding Bingnan to report to the Xinzha Police Station around 1:00 PM in the afternoon. They cooperated with Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate and found that the front building of the house was occupied by Ling Yongyun (Lin Yongyong) from Suzhou. Lin is an actor in the rooftop garden theater of the New World Company, with a wife, five concubines, and three daughters. His wife is also an actress. In March of this year, he bought a local girl named Wang Azhen, 12 years old, for 110 yuan to be his adopted daughter. Because the children usually did things badly, Lin beat her face with a wooden ruler, causing serious injuries. The girl was seen wearing ragged clothes and looking emaciated. After investigation, the Chinese and foreign detectives confirmed the facts and took Lin Yongyong and Wang Azhen to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the case, saying that the defendant was being prosecuted for the crime of interfering with the family under Article 257 of the Criminal Law. After investigation, the Relief Society representative Zhang Yueru filed a complaint, reporting the situation to the police after receiving a phone report. Wang Azhen testified that she was a Shanghai native, 12 years old. She was sold to the defendant as a servant this year by her mother. The defendant often abused her because she did things badly, hitting her face with a wooden ruler. She was not given enough food and had to eat alone. She only ate twice a day and was responsible for pouring water and scrubbing the floor. She only called the defendant couple "Dad" and "Mom". Her other testimony was evasive. The defendant testified that he was an actor at the Xinxin Company Xing Garden. His wife is also an actress. Recently, she became ill and is about to give birth, so she is resting at home. He has one son and three daughters. His son, Dan Sheng, is 12 years old and is currently attending school. He bought Wang Azhen for 120 yuan to be his adopted daughter, intending to marry her to his son Dan Sheng in the future. Wang's father is named Lao Zhang, and he used to be a tea server at the Great World. He met Lao Zhang when he was acting at the Great World. In March of this year, Lao Zhang's home in Zhabei was destroyed by Japanese artillery fire, and his entire family was destroyed. He cried and asked for help, so he paid 120 yuan to buy his daughter Azhen as an adopted daughter. Lao Zhang has now returned to his ancestral home in Anhui and cannot be found. He admitted that he did beat Azhen twice, but he did not know the family rules and violated the law.

And in recent years, the cost of living has been increasing, and the monthly income is limited, so they only rent one front room. They also only eat twice a day. He and his wife eat first, and Azhen and his children eat later. There was really no case of not giving her enough to eat or using her as a servant. He hired Shen Xingxia as a lawyer to defend him, arguing that Lin had a long-term contract with the New World Company, and both parties would suffer if he was detained. Therefore, he requested to be released on bail. Judge Wu Tingqi reviewed the testimony and found that further investigation was necessary. He ordered the defendant to be detained and Wang Azhen to be sent to the Benevolent Child Education Institute for care after a forensic examination. The case was rescheduled for further hearing on the morning of the 19th.

Preemptively Detected by Police

Sixteen Bandits Captured

Huatarn Shangwu of the Hui Police Station recently learned that a large gang of thieves was plotting illegal activities in the concession. The Mother-in-Law and Daughter-in-Law Are Only Five Years Apart 145

An Extremely Modern Girl Suspected

Family History is Also Untrue and Incomplete

Yesterday at 11:30 AM, two young women with alluring looks and modern attire hired a rowboat at the Guangdong Road pier to cross to Pudong. Liu Desheng and Dong Zhanwen happened to see them at the pier and immediately reported it to Water Police No. 85, Shui Hua, who was patrolling the Pudong bank. The two women were taken to the Customs Water Police Station. According to Liu and Dong, the two women were related as mother-in-law and daughter-in-law, the wife and daughter-in-law of their friend Shao Changming, who had both eloped without a trace in April of this year. They were spotted today, and they requested temporary detention so that the Shao father and son could be notified to come and identify them. Upon questioning, the two women stated that one was Zhang Ying, 23 years old from Yixing, who worked as a female supervisor (commonly known as "number one woman") at the Shenxin No. 9 Cotton Mill in Yangshupu. The other was Wang Xiuzhen, 18 years old from Wuxi, also a female worker at the same factory. They became acquainted because of this. The police officers, based on the statements, found it hard to believe that there would only be a five-year age difference between a mother-in-law and daughter-in-law. They immediately sent for the Shao father and son to come to the station for interrogation. At that time, Liu and Dong had already brought Shao Changming and his son Xueying together to the station. Changming stated that he was 46 years old, from Shandong, and formerly served as a patrol officer in the Fourth District Police Station of Zhabei, but was currently unemployed. The defendant, Zhang Ying, was his second wife, and he had a marriage certificate to prove it. He presented the certificate, but the police officers found that it was not stamped, making it difficult to believe. Xueying stated that he was 22 years old and currently a police officer in the Second Station of the Fourth District of Zhabei. Wang Xiuzhen was his wife, and he had a marriage certificate to prove it, but the certificate had been torn up by Xiuzhen and could not be presented. The father and son both claimed that the two defendants had run away from their husbands and requested to take them home for reunion. The police station then questioned Zhang Ying about whether she had a marital relationship with Shao Changming. She replied that she had cohabitated with him for a long time but had now separated from him. Wang Xiuzhen claimed that she did not know Shao Xueying and could not be considered Shao Changming's daughter-in-law. The police station, finding conflicting statements from both parties, decided to transfer the four men and women, along with Liu and Dong who reported them, to the District Court for trial.

A Wronged Spirit Possesses His Brother to Capture the Murderer 146

For a Year, the Deceased's Grievance Remains Unresolved

The Capture of the Murderer Resembles a Myth

Peng Xigen, a tailor from Pengjia Pond, South of Hongqiao Town in Shanghai West, delivered clothes he had made to Tao Sanhai, who worked as a tea vendor in Tao Geng Alley, on the evening of January 2nd of this year. Tao Sanhai had just returned home from outside and mistakenly thought Peng was harassing his wife. He then colluded with neighbors Tao Axin, Tao Haigen, Tao Jigen, and his wife's brother Xu Haigen to beat Peng Xigen to death on the spot. After the incident, the murderers all fled. Only two suspects, Tao Yansheng and Tao Fengxiang, were apprehended. The deceased's father, Peng Huisheng, repeatedly petitioned the court to strictly arrest the murderers and bring them to justice, but Tao Sanhai and his wife remained at large and had not been caught. Unexpectedly, the deceased's younger brother, Peng Zhongbao (23 years old), somehow completely removed his upper body clothing, running around wildly and appearing insane. Huisheng and his wife tried to dissuade him, but Zhongbao sternly rebuked them, saying, "My grievance has been in the underworld for nearly a year. You have not been able to seek justice for me, yet you try to stop me? Now I have found the murderer. My brother can quickly arrest him to prevent his escape!" After speaking, he ran outside, all the way to Zhangjia Bang, west of Caohejing, where he saw Tao Axin fishing in the river. Zhongbao threw himself into the river and captured Axin, then dragged him to the Hongqiao Town Police Station under their jurisdiction, and then transferred him to the First Branch of the Sixth District. After preliminary investigation by Chief Bi, Tao Axin confessed without denial to beating Peng Xigen to death. Chief Bi obtained the confession and prepared a document to transfer the case to the court for trial.

The City Chamber of Commerce Pleads for the Flower and Tree Industry 148

Requests Exemption from Requisitioning Zhao Jia Garden Village Land

Orders the Ministry of Railways to Find a Way to Bypass It

The City Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Third Plenary Session of the Kuomintang yesterday, requesting the National Government to instruct the Ministry of Railways to exempt Zhao Jia Garden Village land from requisition. The original text reads, "To the honorable Third Plenary Session of the Kuomintang: According to a complaint from the Flower and Tree Industry Guild, after the Ministry of Railways requisitioned civilian land to build the Joint Transportation Terminal and changed its plans, it gave up 1,400 mu of land originally designated west of Zhongshan Road and south of Jiaotong Road, and suddenly added the purchase of 700 mu of land east to Zhao Jia Garden, etc., completely requisitioning the village households with thriving populations, flowers, and trees. The flower and tree industry in Shanghai is necessary for society and contributes to the prosperity of the city, and Zhao Jia Garden Branch Lane and other villages are the production area for five-fourths of the flowers and trees. The fields are connected, exceeding a thousand mu, with a staggered view and spring in all seasons. Since cultivation began nearly two hundred years ago, there are millions of large and small flowers and trees. Among them, rare and exotic species have been planted for four or five years, or cultivated for forty or fifty years, before they can yield a small profit. Fathers pass on the business to sons, and grandsons and great-grandsons follow. The entire village has more than 500 households and thousands of people, who depend on it for food and clothing. Even the flowers, fruits, and plants that Shanghai people appreciate rely heavily on Zhao Jia Garden products. However, the Ministry of Railways plans to requisition the historical and valuable gardens of Zhao Jia Garden to build a joint transportation terminal, causing all the villagers to lose their skills and jobs. If they relocate elsewhere, it is important to know that deeply rooted trees are not suitable for the soil and are difficult to plant, unlike rice, sorghum, and wheat, which can be sown anywhere. After the requisition, the land prices in the vicinity will increase, which is beyond the reach of the people. If compensation is given, it is important to know that the cultivation of garden trees is not the work of a day or night. Those who cultivate this have lost their basic livelihood, so how will an eight-member family survive in the next ten years? Since the Qilu War, there have been frequent soldiers, and the survivors of the disaster are scarred. If they are forced to relocate again, they will become refugees. Therefore, we respectfully request you to work together to help and ensure that the Ministry of Railways retracts its order, finds a way to avoid it, alleviates the people's suffering, and maintains their livelihoods." It is important to know that flowers and trees are not easy to transplant and are different from other agricultural products. Even if relocation fees are given, the garden owners abandon their ancestral businesses and still find it difficult to make a living. Although the Ministry of Railways' plan to purchase land for the joint transportation station involves civilian property, the original designation was west of Zhongshan Road and south of Jiaotong Road, where there are no villages and the damage to the people is shallow. When the state undertakes public utilities, it should also consider the livelihoods of the people nearby. But if a way can be found to avoid it, it is always best to choose the lesser of two evils. Now, abandoning the original plan with fewer obstacles, it is replacing it with a densely populated village with centuries of tree planting, leaving them with nowhere to move and no land to transplant. Thousands of residents are on the verge of desperation. In terms of policy, this is also a great violation of public sentiment and shocking. We hereby telegraph to ask for your judgment and respectfully request that you forward it to the government, allowing them to instruct the Ministry of Railways to exempt the entire Zhao Jia Garden village from inclusion in order to maintain the villagers' livelihoods. The people are panicked and await your instructions. Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce respectfully submits this."

About the Kim Cheol Kidnapping Case

Huang Zhanying's Confession 150

The Xinsheng News Agency says that since the Korean resident Kim Cheol was kidnapped, the collusion between Huang Zhanying and the Japanese has made people indignant. Kim's friend Ji Qing even had a major negotiation with Wu Chengyu because of this. On the ninth of this month, Huang sent a letter to Ji, stating his grievances. Ji also published a reply letter, asking Huang to confess. Huang then sent a very detailed confession to Kim Cheol. The details are as follows:

Ji and Huang's Negotiations 151

At 5 PM on the 12th of this month, Wu Chengyu and Ji Qing met at the Guanshengyuan restaurant by appointment to discuss ways to resolve this matter. Wu insisted that the matter should still be resolved by the members of the alliance. Ji said that the case should be reviewed by the Kuomintang branch, the government, and the Shanghai national salvation groups. If there is doubt, they will be sent to court for punishment. Or Huang can send a statement to Kim Cheol, and if Kim deems it to be true, he will publish it in the newspaper to restore Huang's reputation. On the afternoon of the 13th, Huang indeed sent a letter of defense, but Ji pointed out that Huang's address was never disclosed. If he was being assessed, why would his whereabouts be so secretive? On the 14th, Wu Chengyu gathered fellow Cantonese again at his office to discuss. He still did not advocate for public disclosure. Ji Qing said that within this week, if Wu Chengyu and Huang Zhanying did not hand over the documents they took away and come forward publicly, in addition to asking the authorities to arrest them, he would still publish the entire situation in a long article. On the morning of the 15th, Huang Zhanying again asked someone to invite Ji to meet at the Kunlun room of the East Asia Restaurant at 5 PM. Huang said that he had been seriously ill since the incident and had not seen the newspaper, which led to misunderstandings. He asked for ways to explain and restore his reputation. Ji said that there were two ways to handle this case: 1. Explain to Kim Cheol and his son, and after Kim approves, publish it in the newspaper. 2. Conduct a public review by the Party Headquarters and various national salvation organizations, and if there is no suspicion, publish it in the newspaper. However, everything must be public from now on, and after the incident, I have reported it to important agencies. If necessary, public disclosure is even more convincing to the people. Ji then asked about the source of a certain amount of money and a certain item, and Huang answered them all. Now, because the whereabouts of Kim and his son are unknown, it has been temporarily put on hold. However, the letters from all parties regarding this matter are sufficient to prove its true nature.

Huang's Letter to Kim 152

Dear Brother Cheol,

After this incident, I was relieved to learn that you were safe. But you mistakenly believe that I am a traitor, which is extremely unfair and infuriating. Do you want me to be arrested by the Japanese to feel satisfied? The fact that I am not a traitor has already been explained to Brother Ji, but it is still seen in the newspaper. In this way, you are disloyal to a friend, and I have been planning to unite with you day and night for a long time. So, I am unwise to associate with you. Now, for the sake of clarity between us, and according to Brother Ji's words, I would like to clarify the following:

Page 14

Eight questions, two pieces of advice, separately explained. Eight points of clarification: (1) On the day of the incident, I left less than two minutes before it happened, but you strongly said that I left more than forty minutes later. I don't know what your intention is. Moreover, the place is far from the police station. No one blew a whistle when the incident occurred. I risked my life to escape and immediately reported it to the police. The facts can be known by investigation. And I did not come with the police at the time because I was afraid of being abducted or shot by the violent Japanese (I had no gun in my hand at the time, how could I resist?) Then, I would not be able to save myself, let alone save others. (2) It was reported that the evidence had been sent to the Japanese Consulate. I don't know what you saw or heard. If I were a traitor, I would have offered all kinds of documents and covenants to the violent Japanese in order to receive rewards. Why have I been preserving them until now? Because when I moved houses on November 21, the documents entrusted by Brothers Ji and Xu were handed over to my fiancée to be kept in secret, because the star-based agency you invited me to was involved. Otherwise, if this incident had happened and it was searched by the violent Japanese, I would have no freedom even if I made a hundred excuses. (3) If you say that I am acting as a traitor, think about how many times I have been in contact with you in the past few months. In this month alone, I went to Danfenglou about four times, and I also met at Guanshengyuan three or four times (this refers to the times I talked with you, Brother Cheol, there was almost no day when I was alone). These places are all in Chinese territory, and the violent Japanese can easily arrest me. Don't you see that the violent Japanese mistakenly thought that the place was in Chinese territory and arrested me because they had not notified the French police station? It shows that arrests in the Chinese Concession are easier than in the French Concession. In the psychology of the Japanese, if I were colluding with them, how could I not arrange meetings at Danfenglou and Guanshengyuan to act? Moreover, each meeting was arranged the day before, and it was not impossible to do it leisurely. No one is so foolish as to do this at night. (4) As the saying goes, "To kill a snake, first cut off its head; to catch a thief, first catch the king." If I were a traitor, I have been associating with the leaders of your country's revolution, Mr. Qu, since the beginning, and my goal has been to discuss the anti-Japanese actions of the two peoples. The contact has been close. Just to take the recent month as an example, I have been to Hangzhou twice, sightseeing and visiting everywhere. Recently, Zhao came to Songjiang from Hangzhou and asked me to visit. All of this can be inquired of Mr. Zhao and cannot be denied. If I were betraying the alliance and acting as a traitor, I would not seek heavy rewards, but would act to capture the king. From this, it can be seen that the suspicion that I am a traitor is a big mistake. (5) All traitors must first obtain huge amounts of money. In the past few months, I have been running around with you day and night. What is my situation? I think you all know it. I have no clothes for different seasons. I wear summer clothes in spring and winter clothes in summer. The pawn tickets are full of my pockets, which you have seen and can verify. (6) I originally lived on Avenue Joffre. The idea of moving houses came from you. Moreover, the house in Ruyi Lane was personally found and rented by you, and it was your former residence. How could it be difficult for the Japanese to observe this early? There is another reason why it was discovered by the Japanese. After the house was rented in the star, you knew that I had not paid the rent on Avenue Joffre. You can check the two landlords. I cannot move in. At that time, you often came to Ruyi Lane. The key was in your hand. I don't know if you brought anyone there. It is difficult to guarantee that this negligence was detected by the enemy. How can you accuse me on suspicion? (7) Cars are the easiest way to abduct people in Shanghai. Traitors must first conceal their behavior. If I were acting as a spy, I would never bring people into my own house, causing suspicion. Nor would I run away by myself, and not go with the Japanese to point out and arrest people, pretending that I was also arrested in order to conceal myself. Now, because I escaped, I am accused of being a traitor. Then, in the future, revolutionaries must first decide to be arrested by the enemy together to prove that they are not traitors. I am afraid that no comrade will agree with this method. Moreover, if my contact with you was colluding with the enemy, it would be easy to drive around at night or have the Japanese arrest you on the road and put you in the car. Why don't you think about this? How shallow is your view? (8) I also saw in the newspaper that it said that I had moved the house two weeks ago, but nothing was left when I escaped. Upon investigation, it has not been ten days since I moved to Ruyi Lane. How could there be a matter of moving out two weeks ago? This fact is not true. Arbitrarily slandering people can be seen from this. Ten minutes before the incident, you entered my room twice, and all the items were there. If they were moved away, you could have asked. Why use this as a pretext after the incident? Moreover, I have no extra belongings. I only have two suitcases and quilts, etc. for daily use. I have nothing else, as all my comrades know. When I owed rent at Da Jiangnan, Brother Ji guaranteed me. At this time of accusation, this simple luggage was either stolen by robbers or kept by the landlord. In short, when the incident occurred, you entered the room twice. Ask your conscience, did I move anything? This doubt can be broken. My clarification shows that I absolutely did not act as a traitor. Moreover, although my association with you is shallow, I have been running around for the revolution for twenty years. What wealth or power has never changed my integrity, which is well known to all my friends. Now, because of your words, my entire life's reputation and career are ruined. If I go to the underworld, my grievances will be forever buried in the sea. Now I have to raise the following questions: (1) It is said that I claim to be the leader and have printed business cards and documents, and that I have a Western-style house with a monthly rent of 200 taels of silver and a car of my own. Where is the Western-style house, what is the license plate of the car, and where are the printed documents? Unless you immediately go and forge them, this is the first question to answer. (2) The newspaper said that your intention to rent the house in Ruyi Lane and the house in Ximen that you discussed renting before was a consistent policy. You are slandering people. This time the house was rented at your suggestion. How can there be a consistent matter? Is this a way of forcibly incriminating people? This is the second question to be asked. (3) This time it was completely my personal action with you, and it had nothing to do with the alliance. Why do you insist that you believe in Mr. Wu and bring him in out of thin air, causing trouble? Is this adding fuel to the fire and making Mr. Wu angry and arresting me? This is the third question to be asked. As for what can be said to be advice, (1) If you slander me so much, the Chinese and Korean peoples will feel even more difficult. Who will help your country in the future? (2) I am afraid that this kind of behavior of yours is slandering comrades and destroying your personality. You are not worth cherishing, but what about your violation of the alliance? Therefore, if you do not realize your mistakes after Brother Ji's method, what is called "all the past is like yesterday's death, all the future is like today's birth"? Quickly publish a correction so that the people of society can understand right and wrong. I will come out to meet you. Otherwise, for the sake of self-defense, I will have to tell everything to the court, and each will be responsible for his own reputation. I hope you will think twice. Please have your reply sent through Mr. Ji. I wish you all the best, Brother Cheol.

Yours,

Zhan Ying

Xu Xueyu Succeeds as Director of the Telephone Bureau 154

Wei Zengfu's Resignation Approved

Wei Zengfu, Director of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, recently resigned from his post to Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua due to other important matters and plans to recuperate. Minister Zhu approved Wei's earnest resignation and appointed Xu Xueyu, an electrical engineer from the Siemens foreign firm in this city, to succeed him as the director of the telephone bureau. After receiving the order, Xu plans to go to Beijing to meet with Minister Zhu and ask for instructions on everything, and will take office within the next week. Since resigning, Director Wei has ordered his subordinates to rush to complete the handover.

Reader's Advisor 157

Mr. Bao Zizheng writes: I am a person behind the times. I ended up inheriting my family business due to the decline of the rural economy. [Note: symbol for witch doctor] However, my spirit has suffered a great blow. My heart feels as if a sharp blade has pierced it. I have turned the wheels of time and entered the winter of the seventeenth year (presumably of the Republic). Suddenly, I received news from the Civil Affairs Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government about abolishing seven methods of divination, astrology, witch doctors, and geomancy. In my confusion, I had many thoughts. The third provision of the abolition methods stated, "...If, upon the expiration of the deadline, there is still no legitimate occupation, they should be admitted to local factories to learn another trade. In places where no factories have been established, they may be ordered to undertake appropriate work..." (The above was an order from the county government to the public security bureau). Unfortunately, there are no factories locally. Even if I wanted to change professions, I would have no opportunity. The public security bureau does not provide appropriate work, but instead forces us to continue our business as usual. When the wife of the officer has minor illnesses, they ask us to pray for her, but this is only fulfilling our obligations. Beyond this, they are extremely demanding, extorting much illegal money from us every month. We have lived under this coercion for four years, repeatedly trying to find a solution, but without opportunity. Now, fortunately, I have seen your newspaper's reader's advisor and am happy to write out two questions: 1) How to deal with the public security bureau to escape this pain of entanglement? 2) There are about ninety households in our area engaged in this profession, with a total of over five hundred people relying on it for their livelihood. For the sake of the whole group, if we are freed from this, what good methods are there to make a living and embark on a new path? Sir, kind sir, the above two questions concern the life and death of our five hundred people. Please publish them in your newspaper for everyone to discuss.

▲ The reporter notes that the practical problems raised by Mr. Bao not only fully expose the dark side of politics, but also fully expose the dark side of this society, and the questions are extremely valuable for public discussion. Therefore, it is specifically submitted to everyone for public discussion.

Mr. Wu Sijing writes: Here I have a question that I cannot understand, and I would like to ask you to provide me with a more practical and responsible answer. At the same time, there must be many people in society who are suffering as I am. Therefore, I hope you can publish my letter for everyone to discuss together. I am a graduate of the old system high school. Given the current social and economic situation, I am very satisfied that I was able to graduate from the old system high school. Looking back, how many people cannot enter middle school, and how many more cannot enter elementary school. I am truly content. After graduating, I began to enter society to find work. Naturally, I was full of enthusiasm to serve society. I don't cheat, I don't slack off. I want to do what I can and do what I should do. I refuse to compromise with darkness and corruption. I want to preserve my honesty and sincerity. I am confident that my intentions are not wrong, and my future is bright. But, strangely, the maxims and instructions of many wise men, philosophers, and scholars from the East and West have deceived me. I have examined my own behavior, and it is generally consistent with these maxims and instructions. However, I have encountered obstacles. After serving society for three years, I have ultimately failed and become unemployed. My family is very poor. My parents spent a lot of effort to enable me to graduate from middle school. Naturally, I must find a job to survive, but finding a job is not easy. Although I don't have very profound knowledge, I still have considerable skills for making a living. I have the right to demand that society provide me with work. I cannot simply wait to die. Sir, why can't I find a job? I have passed in front of singing halls, dance halls, taverns, and restaurants. They are all elated, never lacking food or drink, followed by wine and meat, and accompanied by prostitutes. Why can't I even get food? I am considered not to have starved to death yet. Sir, look around you, how many people have already starved and become withered wood? Sir, what is the reason for this? Is it fate? I don't believe it. Is it personal destiny? Where is the evidence? Sir, my question here is: First, why can a small number of people have food to eat without relying on their knowledge and ability, while the majority of honest and sincere people with considerable skills for making a living have no food to eat? Sir, I ask you to answer for me.

The reporter notes that I read Mr. Wu's letter in one breath, and a large stone was pressed on my heart again. I can't say anything. Naturally, this is also a question worth discussing, and now it is submitted to everyone for discussion. Mr. Bao writes: My friend, Mr. ×, only studied for one semester in junior high school before being forced by his father to enter business for two years. This spring, due to his father's business failure, he felt quite negative about the business world. Mr. × took the opportunity to ask his father to go to Hangzhou to study at a certain middle school, and his grades were very good. His father was also happy. However, his father recently wanted to revive his business and sent a letter urging him to return to help. Mr. × is by nature purely filial. If he does not return, he fears hurting his father's heart. If he returns, he feels that his knowledge is insufficient and is unwilling to leave school. The conflict of thoughts has led him into a state of distress. Mr. × wrote to me the other day, worrying about this. I am of shallow knowledge and not enough to solve his doubts. I specifically ask you for advice, hoping for detailed guidance so that Mr. × can find his place. Regarding Mr. ×'s family, his father has been in business for many years and accumulated over one hundred thousand yuan. After the failure, he can still be considered well-off. He has three older brothers. The eldest brother is also in business, and the second and third brothers are addicted to bad habits and have no occupation. Because of his two brothers, his father needs him to return to help, but he is also reluctant to force Mr. × not to return.

Reply: Your friend has a "pure and filial nature" and a desire to study, which is very admirable. Your friend's father, because his sons are not virtuous, insists on having your friend drop out of school to help him with his business. His plan is not correct, but his good intentions are understandable. The solution to this problem, in the reporter's view, could be for your friend to earnestly ask a respected and close relative in the clan to explain to your friend's father, making him understand the importance of studying (such as the fact that the second and third sons do not engage in proper occupations is precisely because they did not study, which can also be presented as proof), and to change his stubborn view. Considering the affection between your friend and his father, and your friend's determination to study is so firm, his father will surely be unwilling to unduly violate his wishes.

Chen Tianxiao's National Crisis Painting Exhibition Opens 160

Chairman Lin rewards the first artist

Chen Tianxiao's National Crisis Painting Exhibition, which has been reported in the newspapers for his dedication to saving the country through art during the national crisis, opened today. The Shanghai Charity Association for Relief of Northeastern Refugees sent personnel to manage the drawing of lots to determine the paintings. The venue is on the fourth floor of the Ningbo Fellow Association on Xizang Road. About two hundred works are on display, mostly flowers, followed by landscapes, followed by sketches. Needless to say, the style of his paintings is strong, free, and the momentum is magnificent. His dedication to saving the country through art is particularly a backbone figure in the national crisis. This spring, he held a personal exhibition of national crisis in Yongjia, and used the proceeds to help the refugees of the Battle of Shanghai. Now, he is holding this National Crisis Painting Exhibition to provide relief to the Northeastern refugees. It is said that after the closing of this exhibition, he plans to go to other places to hold personal exhibitions of national crisis in succession, promoting art and striving to save the country. When Chairman Lin heard about this, he sent a letter of encouragement and presented a huge banner with the four characters "Patriotic Spirit", and also selected and collected Chen's painting of peaches. Central committee members and celebrities in Shanghai also made presentations. It is estimated that the opening remarks received included Yu Youren, Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchuo, Chu Minyi, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Guofu, Chen Shuren, Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Xiao Jishan, Wang Qi, Huang Jichen, Shao Yuanchong, Shi Ying, Dong Kang, Wu Kaisheng, Wu Chengyu, Hong Ludong, Lin Chansheng, etc. They are dazzling and beautiful.

Meeting of Supervisors and Directors of the Accountants Association 162

Sold by Laochang on Simalu

Harmful to Youth, Truly Undermining

Water Police Detective Deng Jiagen reported to the French police the night before last that the water police had received a report that someone was specializing in selling spring palace erotic photos at the pier. He immediately arrested one person, who confessed that the organization was located at No. 44 Mill Street under his jurisdiction. Please investigate and arrest them. The head of the police approved the request and sent a detective to go to the place together, arresting Suzhou native Xie Miaosheng and Shanxi native Tang Jinshu, and seizing two rattan boxes of such photos, numbering hundreds. They were taken to the police station. Police lawyer Chen Ming presented the case, stating that the police were prosecuting according to Article 251 of the Criminal Law, and submitted the photos for the record. Xie and Tang both confessed that the photos were actually sent by a Lin surname from outside, and were resold by civilians to Laochang on Simalu (i.e., addicts) for one yuan each, earning a small profit of two jiao. Judge Zhang verified the confession and sentenced Xie Miaosheng and Tang Baoshu in court for the crime of jointly selling obscene pictures, each fined one hundred yuan. If they are unable to pay, two yuan will be used to offset one day of imprisonment. The seized photos were confiscated.

Two Apprentices Come to Shanghai to Seek Work; One Flees with Belongings, the Other Attempts Suicide 166

Human Hearts Are Truly Unfathomable

The Path of Friendship is Fraught with Difficulty

Wang Fukang, 19 years old, and Chen Rongchang, 22 years old, both natives of Ningbo, were formerly apprentices at the Dachangxiang Foreign Goods and Cloth Company in Ningbo. Recently, the company's business was slow, so they were both laid off. A few days ago, Chen Rongchang planned to come to Shanghai to seek work. Knowing that Wang was still unemployed at home, he went to invite him to come to Shanghai together. Wang immediately agreed. After arriving in Shanghai, the two stayed at the Rongji Inn near the Sino-French School on Avenue Metténie in the French Concession. Yesterday morning, around 3:00 AM, Wang awoke from a dream and suddenly realized Chen was not there. He thought he had gone out for urgent needs. However, after waiting until dawn, he still did not see him. He began to suspect something was wrong. He quickly put on his clothes and opened Chen’s suitcase. The money and clothes inside were all gone. Wang was desperate and helpless. He immediately went everywhere to investigate Chen's whereabouts, but to no avail. In a state of dilemma, he suddenly had thoughts of ending his life. Around 4:00 PM, he went to the Dasaban Wharf in Tilanqiao and jumped into the Huangpu River to commit suicide. Fortunately, a Japanese man working at a nearby wharf saw him and quickly devised a way to pull him out of the water. He then reported the incident to the police station, who dispatched an ambulance to send Wang to Tongren Hospital for treatment. However, he had been in the water for too long, and his life was still in danger.

Our country's old, large families cannot be compared with this, and even modern so-called "modern small families" are very different. Because Chinese so-called modern housewives have the extravagant habits of French women but lack their hard-working nature, which often disappoints their husbands. Her words were quite pertinent and worthy of emulation for Chinese family organization. Unfortunately, the speech was lengthy and cannot be fully recorded. It is said that today, Mr. Lu Jizeng, the Dean of Studies at Datia University, will speak on "The Value of Family Education."

Readers' Advice 172

Mr. Bao Zhizheng inquires: I am a person behind the times. Due to the decline of the rural economy, I had no choice but to inherit my family's business as a shaman and doctor. However, my spirit has been greatly affected. My heart feels as if a sharp blade has been thrust into it. I got off the wheel of time and turned back to the winter of the 17th year [of the Republic], and suddenly received the news from the Civil Affairs Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government that it was abolishing the seven methods of divination, astrology, shamanism, physiognomy, and geomancy. In my chaos, I have had many feelings. Article 3 of the abolition methods states that "... those who do not have proper jobs after the deadline should be taken into factories established by the local government to learn a new profession. Localities that do not have factories may order them to take on corresponding work..." (The above is an order from the county government to the Public Security Bureau). Unfortunately, there is no factory in my area. Even if I want to change professions, I have no opportunity, and the Public Security Bureau does not give me corresponding work. Instead, it orders me to continue operating as usual. When his wife has a minor illness, they also ask us to pray for her. But this is fulfilling an obligation. Apart from this, he extorts us in every possible way, seizing many illegal fees from us every month. We have lived under this kind of coercion for four years, repeatedly trying to find a way to deal with it, but without opportunity. Now, fortunately, I saw your newspaper's Reader's Advice column, and I am happy to write out two questions: 1. How to deal with the Public Security Bureau to get rid of this painful constraint? 2. There are about 90 such practitioners in our area, and the total number of people living on this is more than 500. For the sake of everyone, if we are freed, what good ways are there to make a living and step into a new path? Kind sir, these two questions are related to the life and death of our 500 people. Please publish them in your newspaper for everyone to discuss.

▲ The reporter notes that the practical problems raised by Mr. Bao not only fully expose the dark side of politics, but also fully expose the dark side of this society. Moreover, the questions are of great value for public discussion. Now, they are specifically submitted for public discussion.

Mr. Wu Sijing writes: Here, I have a question that I cannot understand no matter how much I think about it, and I would like to ask you, sir, to give me a relatively practical and responsible answer. At the same time, there must be many people in society who have experienced the same pain as I have. Therefore, I hope that you, sir, can publish my letter and let everyone discuss it together. I am a graduate of the old high school system. Considering the current social and economic situation, I am already very satisfied that I was able to graduate from the old high school system. Looking back, how many people cannot enter middle school, and even more people cannot enter elementary school. I am really already content. After graduation, I started to enter society and look for a job. Naturally, I am serving society with 120,000 points of enthusiasm. I do not cheat, I do not slack, and I will do what I should do to the best of my ability. I am not willing to compromise with darkness and corruption. I want to preserve my honesty and sincerity. I am confident that my intentions are not wrong and that my future is bright. But, strangely, the maxims and famous teachings of many sages and scholars, both Chinese and Western, have deceived me. I have examined my own behavior and found that it generally does not violate these maxims and famous teachings. However, I have run into obstacles. After serving society for three years, I have finally failed and become unemployed. My family is very poor. My parents also spent a lot of effort for me to graduate from middle school. Naturally, I must find a job to survive, but how easy is it to find a job? Although I do not have any profound knowledge, I still have considerable skills to make a living. I have the right to demand that society give me work. I cannot wait to die of starvation. Sir, why can't I find a job? When I pass by singing halls, dance halls, restaurants, and taverns, everyone is excited and happy. Those who are not full eat and drink, followed by wine and meat, and then singing girls serving wine. But why can't I even get a meal? I am still not starved to death. Sir, look around you, how many people are already so hungry that they have become a withered tree? Sir, what is the reason for this? Heaven? I do not believe it. Individual destiny? Where is the evidence? Sir, my question here is: 1. Why can a small number of people have food to eat without relying on their knowledge and ability, while the majority of honest, sincere people with considerable skills to make a living do not have food to eat? Sir, I am Lei Jia, please help me answer this.

The reporter notes: I read Mr. Wu's letter in one breath, and another big stone was suddenly pressed on my heart, and I could not say anything. Naturally, this is also a question worth discussing. Now, it is submitted for everyone to discuss. Bao Jun inquires: My friend Mr. × only studied in junior high school for one semester before his father forced him to enter business for two years. This spring, due to his father's business failure, he felt quite negative about the business world. Mr. × took the opportunity to ask his father to go to Hangzhou to study at a certain middle school. His grades were very good, and his father was also happy. However, his father recently wanted to revive his business and sent a letter asking him to return to help. Mr. × is pure and filial by nature. If he does not return, he fears hurting his father's heart, but if he returns, he feels that his knowledge is insufficient and is unwilling to leave school. The conflict in his thoughts has made him fall into a state of depression. Mr. × wrote to me a few days ago, worried about this. I am ignorant and cannot enlighten him, so I especially ask you, sir, for guidance so that Mr. × can find what is right for him. Regarding Mr. ×'s family, his father had accumulated more than 100,000 yuan from business for many years. After the failure, he is still considered to be well-off. He has three elder brothers. The eldest brother is also in business, and the second and third brothers are addicted to bad habits and have no jobs. Because his two brothers are like this, it is one reason why his father must ask him to return to help, and it is also a reason why Mr. × is reluctant to return.

Reply: Your friend is "pure and filial" and has the ambition to learn, which is very admirable. Your friend's father wants to order your friend to abandon his studies and help him in business because his sons are not good. Although his plan is not very correct, his good intentions are excusable. In the reporter's opinion, the solution to this problem is whether your friend can ask a more prestigious and amiable person from your relative clan to explain to your friend's father and make him understand the importance of learning (such as the reason why the second and third sons do not engage in proper work is because they did not study, which can also be brought up as proof), and to turn back his stubborn opinion. I think with your friend's feelings for his father and your friend's ambition to study being so firm, his father will definitely not bear to disobey his wish.
