Minister of Industry and Commerce Chen Gongbo Goes to Jinling University to Give a Speech 178

On the day before the Premier's Memorial Week, Jinling University specially invited Chen Gongbo, the Minister of Industry and Commerce, to come to the school to give a speech. The topic was "Dynamic Materialism"

Chen said that after the Revolution of 1911, the Chinese people initially believed that ideals could save the country, but then tended towards fatalism. Recently, they have returned to fantasy. After the September 18th Incident, the Chinese people have all fallen into a state of hesitation. To seek a way out for thought, one must first not doubt oneself, but develop outward from oneself as a starting point. Chen admitted that his personal thought belongs to the materialistic aspect, so he opposes causality and fatalism, and proves that religion, ethics, conscience, psychology, and artistic principles often change due to material changes. All human thoughts originate from matter, and matter is constantly changing, so one should promote personal life with a dynamic materialistic view, and should not take the path of empty morality, which makes everyone fall into an atmosphere of double personality. At the same time, one can seek the completion of the actual responsibilities between people and make the common living standard of the masses.

The Central Organization Committee of the Third Plenary Session Proposes 179

Reforms of Higher Education Content

National University Colleges Merged or Closed

Severely Restricting Private Establishment of Universities

Focusing on Colleges of Agriculture, Industry, Commerce, Medicine, and Science

Cheng Tianfang Proposes a Proposal to Determine Educational Goals and Reform the Educational System 180

Nanjing, 16th Telegram At the Third Plenary Session, Cheng Tianfang proposed a proposal to determine educational goals and reform the educational system, which is divided into three items: A. National Education, seven items for B. Production Education, five items for C. Teacher Education, and seven items for D. Talent Education.

The Central Organization Committee proposes the following measures for reforming higher education: 1. Universities should be established by the Ministry of Education. Universities established by provincial and municipal governments, organizations, and private individuals should be closed down, except for colleges of agriculture, industry, medicine, and science that have special achievements. 2. National universities should be temporarily established in Beijing, Shanghai, Guangzhou, Wuchang, and Xi'an. The Ministry of Education should consider merging or closing the original national universities and independent colleges based on the situation. 3. National universities should be divided into colleges of arts, sciences, law, agriculture, industry, commerce, medicine, and pharmacy. All education colleges should be merged into the college of arts and changed to the department of education. 4. National universities should have at least three colleges. National Peiping Normal University should be closed immediately. 5. Provincial and municipal governments may establish independent colleges based on local conditions. 6. Provincial and municipal governments and private colleges should be limited to establishing colleges of agriculture, industry, commerce, medicine, and science. 7. Provincial and municipal governments, organizations, and private individuals may not establish colleges of arts and law. Those that have been established should be merged into national universities or ordered to close down. 8. In all public universities and independent colleges, the courses in literature, philosophy, and social sciences should have domestic teaching materials and set up special subjects or be incorporated into related subjects as much as possible for teaching. 9. The Ministry of Education should hold graduation exams once or twice a year for all public and private universities and independent colleges. 10. The Ministry of Education should detail the principles and methods of moral education for universities and independent colleges. 11. Based on the above measures, revise the current university organization law and all laws and regulations concerning higher education.

Special

For the Sake of Middle Schools Nationwide (II) 181

— Liao Maoru

Based on experience, educational theory, and modern trends, the teaching hours in middle schools should never be increased. So, what is the basis for the Ministry of Education's resolute increase?

The Ministry of Education believes that after the time for each subject is increased, the students' level will definitely improve. However, the opposite is true in practice. For schools that do not study seriously, it is useless to require 35 hours of class per week, let alone 48 hours, because teachers can arbitrarily skip classes and students can skip classes for no reason. Even in class, they are aware of the classroom hearing picture described by Mr. Zhuang Yixuan. There is no specified work on a daily basis, and there is no strict method of checking. Teachers and students are all making a living in the word "muddle along". In schools that study seriously, each subject has work for students to do every day, there are temporary tests every week, monthly exams every month, and a general review/term exam once a semester. Most teachers are patient and try their best to make sure that students benefit as much as possible. In this kind of school, taking more than 20 hours of classes per week is already very busy, because students also have sports and group education activities. After the class hours are increased, teachers have to reduce the assigned work, and students have to reduce the time for self-study. The result is a decline in level.

To summarize the above, the effects of increasing teaching time are: 1. Insufficient self-study time, 2. Lack of exercise time, 3. Hindering extracurricular activities, 4. Lowering the level of each subject.

2. Cancelling the Liberal Arts and Science Divisions is Too Unrealistic 182

The first school system prescribed in our country was not implemented. The second school system promulgated stipulated that all middle school courses were fixed and did not divide into subjects. In the Xuantong period, middle schools began to divide into liberal arts and science. In the early years of the Republic of China, although there was a method to cancel the division of liberal arts and science, it was soon restored. During the period when schools were established in the Qing Dynasty, the number of middle school students was very small, and the level of mathematics and science was not very high. Most people who entered middle school hoped to go to college, so it was still possible to force them to not divide into subjects. However, in the Xuantong period, the method of dividing into liberal arts and science had already been hotly debated. At present, the number of middle school students increases year by year, so the aspirations and abilities are more varied. Moreover, the level of mathematics and science for college entrance exams has been greatly improved compared to before (Jiaotong University can be taken as an example). Now, regardless of the ability and aspirations of young people, they are all taught to use the same time to learn the same teaching materials. The dull ones sigh in vain, and the excellent ones are restricted. How can this work?

I guess the Ministry of Education thinks that middle school courses are all basic and that every student should learn them, and no student can't learn them, so fixing everything is not a problem. This view is too far from reality. Elementary school courses can be viewed in this way, but junior high school is not entirely the case, and high school is even harder to say. Students who are close to mathematics and science (especially arithmetic) have strong interest and talent. The books are deeper and they learn faster, and they do not think it is hard. Students who are close to literature get headaches when they see arithmetic. It is already very difficult to teach them to learn algebra, geometry, and trigonometry. It is only possible for them to wait for the next life if they are asked to learn advanced algebra, analytic geometry, and do practical exercises. Furthermore, in the case of female students, there are actually more difficulties. At present, almost two-thirds or more of the students in girls' middle schools are studying liberal arts. To suddenly change them to learn mathematics and science and meet the standards set by the Ministry is truly like trying to catch fish by climbing a tree.

Or the Ministry of Education believes that ordinary middle schools are exclusively for preparing students to go to university (whether this concept is reasonable will not be discussed for the time being), so people who enter middle school have to prepare for college entrance exams and have to prepare for the courses for college entrance exams. I don't know that in this era of world chaos and famine, who can decide what will happen in two or three years. If you survey the students in the first year of high school and ask them if they will go to college after graduation, at least 50% are undecided. Even if they have definite aspirations, they still have to change them temporarily. Those who go to college suddenly go to work, and those who go to work suddenly go to college. Human affairs are uncertain, and this is generally the case. Therefore, it is necessary to discuss that there is really no need for everyone to learn advanced mathematics. People who enter ordinary middle schools will not all go to university, and those who go to university will not all apply for science and engineering. Since the need is like this and the facts are like that, why does the Ministry of Education want to cancel the liberal arts and science subjects to make it difficult for young people who are not interested and do not have the aspirations? It is not only making it difficult for young people who are not interested and do not have the aspirations, but even young people who are interested in mathematics and science are subject to various restrictions and cannot fully develop their special abilities. This is such a pity.

Junior High School Curriculum Standards (8)

Animals 183

1. Goals

(1) To understand the relationship between animals and human life.

(2) To understand the morphology, structure, and physiological functions of animals.

(3) To understand the outline of animal classification and its adaptation to the environment.

(4) To have the knowledge of loving beneficial animals and eliminating harmful animals.

(5) To have the preliminary training of collecting and raising animals, and at the same time cultivate their interest in research and appreciation.

2. Time Allocation 184

To be taught in the first academic year of junior high school, with two hours of lectures per week. The practice is to be guided by the teachers in charge and held by students outside of class for two hours per week.

Section 3: Teaching Material Outline 185

(1) Mammal Class: (1) Cat, (2) Macaque, (3) Dog, (4) Cow, (5) Horse, (6) Camel, (7) Elephant, (8) Finless porpoise (Cetacea), (9) Rat, (10) Mouse (or hedgehog or hedgehog), (11) Bat, (12) Shark carp, (13) Kangaroo, (14) Platypus, etc. (15) Summary of Mammal Class. "Note": When describing the structure and physiology of cats, it is advisable to make a comparison with the human body.

(2) Bird Class: (1) Chicken or pigeon, (2) Eagle, (3) Woodpecker, (4) Swallow, (5) Crane, (6) Duck, (7) Ostrich, etc. (8) Summary of Bird Class.

(3) Reptile Class: (1) Turtle, (2) Snake, (3) Lizard, (4) Fish, etc. (5) Summary of Reptile Class.

(4) Amphibian Class: (1) Frog, (2) Salamander (or Giant Salamander, etc.), (3) Summary of Amphibian Class.

(5) Fish Class: (1) Carp or crucian carp, (2) Fish, (3) Lungfish, (4) Shark, (5) Summary of Fish Class.

(6) Summary of Vertebrates

(7) Insect Class: (1) Silkworm moth, (2) Rice borer, (3) Butterfly, (4) Locust, (5) Bee, (6) Ant, (7) Mosquito, (8) Fly, (9) Longhorn beetle, (10) Cicada, (11) Dragonfly, (12) Egg, (13) Silverfish, etc. (14) Summary of Insect Class.

(8) Arthropod: (1) Shrimp (or crab), (2) Spider, (3) Centipede, (4) Summary of Arthropods.

(9) Mollusk: (1) Mussel, (2) Squid, (3) Snail, (4) Summary of Mollusks.

(10) Echinoderm: (1) Starfish, (2) Sea urchin, (3) Sea cucumber, etc. (4) Summary of Echinoderms.

(11) Annelid: (1) Earthworm, (2) Leech, (3) Summary of Annelids.

(12) Roundworm: (1) Ascaris, (2) Summary of Roundworms.

(13) Flatworm: (1) Tapeworm, Summary of Flatworms.

(14) Coelenterate: (1) Hydra, (2) Jellyfish, (3) Coral, etc. (4) Summary of Coelenterates.

(15) Sponge: (1) Sponge, (2) Summary of Sponges.

(16) Protozoa: (1) Paramecium, (2) Amoeba, etc. (3) Summary of Protozoa.

(17) Comparison of Vertebrates and Invertebrates.

(18) The phenomenon of life and its characteristics.

(19) The position of mankind in nature.

Note: The following points should be noted when compiling teaching materials:

(1) The classification order should be the warp for compiling teaching materials, and various animals that are commonly seen and most closely related to life should be the weft.

(2) Morphological structure is closely related to life function. The morphology in the teaching material must also discuss physiology. All aspects of circulation, respiration, digestion, excretion, secretion, reproductive sensation, and action need to be developed.

(3) Comparison is a kind of scientific method, which can enable students to understand what they have learned. The compilation of teaching materials should pay attention to the similarities and differences of various animals, and the same and similar points, and use it to show the traces of animal evolution.

(4) The adaptation of a certain animal to the environment and its benefits to mankind should be mentioned everywhere in the teaching material.

(5) For representative animals of each class or order, collect materials as detailed as possible, and others can be simplified. Animals that are not easy to obtain specimens, such as marine animals that are not easily obtained inland, can also be simplified.

(6) For the endemic animals of this country or native land, the materials should be as rich as possible.

(7) For animals that are appearing at the time, the preparation of materials focuses on the living conditions of the animal at that time.

Section 4: Summary of Implementation Methods 186

(1) Operation requirements: (1) Observation, (2) Experiment, (3) Collection, (4) Record, (5) Drawing, (6) Reasoning.

(2) Teaching points: Choose animals that are commonly seen and most closely related to life as models to discuss their morphology, physiology, ecology, classification, and benefits and harms to humans. All facts that can be obtained through observation or experimentation must be given the opportunity to observe and experiment automatically, and the teacher is in a position to guide.

Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education Compiles Supplementary Teaching Materials for the January 28th Incident 187

So that all schools can uniformly adopt them

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, in view of the importance of the January 28th Incident to the country and the nation, in order to instill national education and enable primary school students to understand the course of the January 28th Incident, previously ordered all schools to send their self-compiled supplementary teaching materials to the bureau for review and compilation. The collection has now been completed. The compilation section of the bureau has sorted out the teaching materials separately, selected the important ones, and compiled one volume of supplementary teaching materials for senior high school, junior high school, and elementary school, so that all schools can uniformly adopt them.

The new location of Shanghai County is in the North Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway. The location is ideal, the transportation is convenient, and the environment is particularly good. Xinhua Art College, the College of Political Science and Law, Zhengfeng College, Guanghua Middle School, and other schools in this city have also successively sent letters to the Shanghai County Government requesting the purchase of foundations near the new administration area for the construction of new buildings. Recently, the county government has sent personnel to find locations, and those who have succeeded are Xinhua Art College with 30 acres and the College of Political Science and Law with 20 acres. The other schools, such as Guanghua Zhengfeng, are also in negotiations.

Municipal Education Bureau Orders Approval to Restore Maicun Elementary School 193

Maicun Elementary School in Jiangwan, since the January 28th Incident, all school buildings have been burned down. It has been suspended for more than half a year. Xiangmin Hou Jinxiang and others in the district, in view of the large number of out-of-school children in the vicinity after the school was suspended, voluntarily used four houses and a piece of open space as the school buildings, and requested the Seventh District Education Association to forward the request to the Municipal Education Bureau for approval to restore it. Now it is learned that the Municipal Education Bureau has ordered the Seventh District Education Association to approve the restoration. The original order said, "It is reported that Hou Jinxiang is willing to lend four remaining houses and a piece of open space for the application of Maicun Elementary School. He is enthusiastic about education and is worthy of praise. However, there are only two months left in this semester. The restoration of Maicun Elementary School should be reviewed and handled in a comprehensive manner at the beginning of the next semester. This order."

Performance Schedule in Hangzhou 211

Continuous Matches for Three Days Starting from the 30th

Basketball, Soccer, Tennis, and Race Walking

Commercial News

Financial Gold Market Swap Storm 213

An Unprecedented Peak of 819.8 Taels Appeared

The Difference of 13 Taels Strong, the Ending Contains Latent Soft Signs

Swap Almost at Par 214

Yesterday, there were still drastic changes, the storm was strong, and it was difficult to restrain. It happened to be the formal swap day, so the market started trading half an hour earlier, at 8:30 AM. However, the firms started even earlier, before 8:00 AM. The January-to-February swap was still being offered by short sellers, initially at 1.5 mace per tael, but trading was limited and immediately declined, with many parties swapping at less than 1 tael. Then it was only a few qian, and when the listing was announced, it was swapped at par. Hengxing and others traded quickly, and later many parties were willing to swap out, causing the short side to instead offer a premium of 1-2 qian, then immediately swapped at par. This was because the local spot market was quite plentiful, with about 4-5,000 taels, which affected the long side. An investigation found that the Dalian group had mixed long and short positions, but no large amounts. Yuanmao Yong, Tongtaichang, Yifeng, and Yongjun held short positions. As for the long side, there were Hengxing, Yifeng (about 6,000 bars in total), Tongfeng, Hengyingfeng, Hengqian, Changxiang, Chunyuan, Yong, etc. Many firms had not finished swapping, almost no one was entering or exiting January, and most were switching to February, with the listed prices shifting to February.

February's Complex Market Conditions 215

Yesterday, February's market was chaotic, and traders were at a loss, with fluctuations of 3-4 taels. However, the daily range was a strong 13 taels, and the result was a latent softening, falling more than 3 taels. Brokers still had no large transactions. The initial opening was stable, but the silver market and British silver fell continuously, American silver did not move, and exchange rates continued to rise. Fortunately, forward silver prices and American cotton both saw declines, so the gold price did not fall. Later, after a slight setback, the exchange rate rebounded slightly, reaching a peak of 819.8 taels, a record since the opening of the commercial market. However, as the exchange rate eased and there were rumors that large amounts might rebound, Hengxing and other long positions sold off, shocking the market and causing it to weaken suddenly, falling by more than 10 taels. The market's turbulence did not stop, and it went from firm to weak, eventually reaching 806.5 taels, still due to strong selling pressure. Finally, it eased slightly.

Morning Market's Sharp Rise and Fall 216

From the morning at 8:30 AM, February opened at 812.2 taels, then fluctuated by 2 taels. Hengyu and Dadecheng sold, while Yongfeng and Hengchang Yongze bought. After 8:45 AM, Wanxingshunli and retail investors sold, and there was talk of swap long positions offering premiums, so it fell by more than 2 taels. At 9:00 AM, it was 808.2 taels. Then, Huabi absorbed January US dollars at 93.75 to 87.5, and January British silver absorbed 31.25. Yuanmao, Yongzhifeng, Yongfuxing, and Yongyuantai all bought, and March British silver was also absorbed by Huabi at 31.25. January US dollars were traded at 68.75, causing the gold price to jump 7 taels, reaching 15 taels around 9:30 AM. HSBC's listing announced that British silver was flat and American silver rose by 12.5, at 13.5 taels at the time. Afterwards, it gradually rose by more than 6 taels, but there was a 1-2 tael pullback, and the exchange market strengthened further. February US dollars were traded at 75, and March British silver was only settled at 25. On the trading floor, Zhifengyong, Yifengyong, Yonglai bought aggressively. By 10:00 AM, British silver had been reduced by 12.5, and US dollars by 37.5, causing the gold price to reach an unprecedented new price of 19.8 taels. Afterwards, although the exchange rate was further reduced, the domestic market was not tight, so the price fell back by 1-2 taels. Suddenly, it was heard that Hengyu was selling for Hengxing, and Hengchang, Yongfuyu, Qingfa, Yongfuchang, Futaiheng, Dadecheng, Zhaofengchang, Yifengyong, Qianchangxiang, Wanxingshunli, and others were selling heavily. Hengxing also followed suit, until 11:00 AM, it broke the 10-tael mark, eventually reaching 808.1 taels. It was unexpected, and the changes were rapid. Afterwards, Zhifengyong and Yifengyong bought, pulling it up by 3 taels to 11 taels at 11:30 AM. Then, it was suppressed by 3 taels because March US dollars were available for sale at 28.0625 yuan, settled at 28 yuan, and Hongkang Yong, Yuanheng, Yuanmao, and Zhaofengchang sold off, immediately retreating to 8 taels. Hengxing and Hengyu bought slightly, and at 11:50 AM, it was 10.03 taels. Goods came out, and the noon closing was 9.7 taels.

(The After-Market Turned from Firm to Weak) The after-market opened at 11 taels, then from 11.8 taels to 10.5 taels. Qianchangxiang, Yuanxingyong, and retail investors bought, immediately reaching 12.8 taels, and January British silver was traded at 1.825. Later, Yuanchun, Yuantai, and Yuanmao Yong sold off, falling back by 3 taels, until 3:00 PM, it was 809.7 taels. Suddenly, Hengyu and Chunyuan Yong bought, Andar absorbed March US dollars at 28 yuan, and Holland absorbed 93.75, so it picked up by more than 4 taels in ten minutes, reaching 14 taels. In an instant, it fell back by more than 4 taels, and sellers were active. At 3:40 PM, it was 809.6 taels. Soon, it rose again to 12.2 taels, Chunyuan Yong and Hongxingyong bought, and HSBC absorbed March 93.75 as well. Since the sellers were active, at 4:00 PM, it was around 10 taels. Then it weakened further, and Fuxingyong, Zhifengyong, Yuhe, Hengyu, Hengxing, and others sold off in droves (and it was rumored that the goods were Hengxing's receipts), so the price frequently went downstream, until at 4:20 PM, it eventually reached 806.5 taels. Afterwards, Andar absorbed March 28 yuan again, Hengyu and others bought, and in three or four minutes, it rose by 3 taels to 809.5 taels. However, Hongkang Yong and general retail investors were eager to sell, and it was seen at 808.2 taels again. At that time, it rose again to 809 taels. By the time the market closed at 4:30 PM, it was 808.4 taels, approximately 3.5 taels lower than the previous day. Considering the flat swap, the daily range was a maximum of 19.8 taels and a minimum of 806.5 taels, a difference of 13.3 taels. The net decrease was 8.5 taels.

(Long Positions Suppressed by 12-13 Taels) The listed price of US dollars was raised by 12.5, resulting in 869 taels, a discount of 54 taels. It was then reduced by 37.5, resulting in 881 taels, a discount of 62-63 taels to 73 taels. In the afternoon, it was 70 taels or so, then 67 taels. The result was 73 taels, an increase of 12-13 taels compared to the previous day. The ledger showed 11 taels for this month, 10 taels for January and February, a supplementary payment of 8 taels, and 6 taels in the afternoon.

(Heavy Trading by Various Firms) Trading on the trading floor was chaotic and erratic. Statistics showed that Yuanmao Yong, Wanxing, Yongfeng, Yuantai, Zhifengyong, Yuanchun, Fuxingyong, Hengchangyong, Bingxing, and Yuhe all bought. Hengyu initially bought and then sold (it was heard that it was selling for Hengxing). Fuyu bought and then sold. Shunli, Yuanheng, Dadecheng, Zhaofengchang, Futaiheng, Fuchang, and Qianchangxiang all sold. In the afternoon, Qianchangxiang, Hengchangyong, Shunli, and Futaiheng all bought. Yuantai, Wanxing, Yuanmao Yong, Zhifengyong, Hongkangyong, and Yuanchun all sold off. The rest was mixed. The Dalian group had a total of 2,500-2,600 bars, roughly squared. The Guang group, Hengxing, traded a total of more than 100 bars on its own account and sold more than 500 bars. Yifeng had a small number of entries and exits.

Erratic Fluctuations in Foreign Exchange 217

|Listing Market Changes|

Yesterday in the silver market, British silver continued to fall, while American silver remained unchanged. The same was true for private telegrams. The upward trend in exchange rates did not stop, increasing by 25 to 68.75. However, the local exchange market fluctuated from time to time. HSBC's initial listing showed British silver flat and American silver rising by 12.5. French and German also rose, and the rest remained unchanged. At 10:15, it suddenly reduced by half a grade, with British silver at 12.5 and American silver at 37.5. The others also followed suit, except for Hong Kong, which did not change. The domestic market initially showed British silver firm and then flat, and it remained stable in the afternoon, eventually shrinking by 0.0625 compared to the day before. American silver was loose in the morning and then strong, weakened at noon, and was firm and then flat in the afternoon, leveling out with the previous day. This was because the exchange rate continued to rise, and the gold market trended upward and then downward. Trading in various banks was quite lively, with more than 100,000 pounds of British silver being traded, with gold firms selling first and then buying. Various banks also traded against each other, and about 800,000-900,000 yuan of American silver was traded, with the pre-market buying and the post-market selling, with occasional hedging transactions. Banks such as Huabi bought strongly, and Andar absorbed in the afternoon, but there were also many who traded against each other. In summary, British silver was tight both openly and secretly, and American silver was initially raised in the listing and then reduced, with the domestic market leveling out.

Large Bars Down to 17 Pence 218

A Reuters dispatch from London on the 16th reported that large bars of silver frequently shrank, with closing prices for near and far futures both at 17 pence, a reduction of 0.0625 for near futures and 0.125 for far futures compared to the previous day. The exchange rate between British and American currency opened at 3 yuan, 3 jiao, and 2.5 fen.

Silver Yuan Market Remains Lifeless 219

Yesterday, the silver yuan market remained stable due to a lack of demand. Banks had no significant appetite for buying or selling yuan, and transactions between money shops were also limited. As a result, although the market was not entirely calm, it was vastly different from normal.

(Static and Dynamic Overnight Interest) The overnight interest rate for silver yuan in the morning market was 7 qian, 1 fen, 4 li, 3 hao, 7 hu, and half a si. The afternoon market was 7 qian, 1 fen, 4 li, and the result was the same as the previous day, showing the market's stability. The overnight interest rate for silver was 3 fen in both the morning and afternoon markets, the same as the previous day, with no change throughout.

(Rise in Auxiliary Jiangnan and Guangdong Fractional Currency) Jiangnan fractional yuan was 6 qian, 2 fen, 4 li, 8 hao, 7 hu, and half a si in the morning market, a decrease of 6 hao, 2 hu, and half a si compared to the previous day's afternoon market. The afternoon market suddenly increased by 1.5 li and strengthened, reaching 6 qian, 2 fen, and 6.5 li. Transactions were 7,500 jiao in the morning market and 10,500 jiao in the afternoon market. Guangdong fractional yuan was 6 qian, 2 fen, and half a li in the morning market and 6 qian, 2 fen, and 0.875 li in the afternoon market. Transactions were 95,000 jiao in the morning market and 75,000 jiao in the afternoon market. Copper coins increased by 1,200 wen, reaching 394,700 wen.

(Inflow and Outflow of Silver Yuan Remain Flat) Yesterday, banks received more than 2 million in silver drafts from Chinese merchants, more than 1.2 million from foreign merchants, more than 2.4 million in special drafts, more than 900,000 in pledged transactions, and more than 5 million in various cargo tax drafts. 900,000 was withdrawn from the warehouse. Money shops and silver guilds received more than 28 million in drafts, and more than 3.9 million in scheduled drafts. Various exchange drafts received more than 600,000, and cash receipts were more than 800,000. For silver yuan, drafts were made out for 815,000 in the morning market and 570,000 in the afternoon market. Banknotes were 55,000 in the morning market and 40,000 in the afternoon market. Over-the-counter banknotes were 40,000 in the morning market and 65,000 in the afternoon market. Checks were 30,000 in the morning market and 45,000 in the afternoon market. Bank transactions were 600,000 in the morning market and 400,000 in the afternoon market. Inflows and outflows of silver yuan accounts between banks were more than 1.5 million. Inflows and outflows of money shop banknotes were more than 1.1 million. Money shops and silver guilds received more than 8.3 million in drafts, and more than 1.7 million in scheduled silver yuan drafts. Inflows and outflows of overnight silver yuan loans were more than 1.8 million. Small money shops transacted more than 600,000, with a net balance of 400,000. Silver yuan pledge transactions were 700,000.

Review of London Large Bar Stock Market and Exchange Rates 224

(Stock Market) A London dispatch on the 15th stated that the stock market gradually improved last week due to the somewhat clarified issue of war debts, and the Ministry of Finance's memorandum did not require additional special taxes to reorganize finances. In this new atmosphere, all trends were positive except for Gold Edge Bonds, which were somewhat restricted due to debt funds. German bonds also saw progress due to the recent resolution of the issue of joining the Geneva Disarmament Conference. Other foreign bonds showed slight progress, but then the trend became uncertain. Japanese bonds were calm, and Chinese bonds remained stable. In the industrial sector, although commerce was sluggish, values were stable. Oil stocks fluctuated due to the Anglo-Persian oil rights dispute, and mining stocks were strong. Rubber stocks were stagnant.

(Foreign Exchange) Gold pounds were steadily improving, and their rise was further accentuated by the fall in the franc due to the fall of the French cabinet. Chinese exchange rates were weak due to silver shrinkage, and Japanese exchange rates were uncertain.

(Large Bars) Mocatta & Goldsmid reported that although there were not many sellers in the silver market last week, the price of silver fell due to the rebound in gold pounds and the closing of long positions. Transactions were small, with some selling from India, China, and the United States. China bought slightly at low prices, and the current price is very small.

Guangdong and Zhejiang Merchants Actively Purchase Spot Yarn 226

Marked Yarn Futures Jumped Wildly in the Second and Third Sessions

The yarn market was flat and weak in the morning, with a tendency to soften, due to the decline of American cotton and a pause in sales. Unexpectedly, the second and third sessions in the afternoon saw a wild jump, with merchants from Guangdong and Zhejiang in South China actively making purchases. At the same time, the price of raw cotton trended upward, boosting confidence. The sudden surge caused considerable tension. The middle two months of marked yarn surpassed the previous day's high price. The yarn market is being driven by real demand, and there is still upward momentum in the future.

(Significant Progress in Marked Yarn) In the morning session for marked yarn, the market opened with a downward trend in American cotton and a flat gold market. There was a lack of buyers in the market, and prices for various months fell by 3, 5, and 6 cents. The afternoon session opened flat, but the second and third sessions suddenly surged due to strong sales. Prices for various months increased by 1.1, 1.2, 1.4, and 1.5 cents. Cotton Market Becoming Increasingly Tight 228

│Severe Shortage of Spot Goods, Difficulty Procuring Foreign Cotton│

The cotton market was calm in the morning due to the decline of American cotton and a flat gold market. Unexpectedly, in the second and third sessions in the afternoon, prices suddenly soared, and the situation was quite bullish, with short sellers appearing panicked. The reason cited was a severe shortage of spot goods and difficulties in procuring foreign cotton. At the same time, speculators unanimously inclined to purchase, causing the market to become increasingly high.

(Non-Industry Players Heavily Absorbing Forward Cotton) In the morning session for Zheng marked cotton, the market opened flat due to the fall of American cotton, with no fluctuations in prices for various months. In the afternoon, the second and third sessions saw a wild jump, with prices rising in all months by 4, 5, and 6 cents. The reason cited was that Chinese cotton production was estimated to be more than 2.7 million dan less than the previous estimate. In general, non-industry players were heavily absorbing forward contracts, causing the market to become even tighter. The total transaction volume for the day was 119,300 dan. Dachangcheng sold 3,800 dan, Dafu 1,900 dan, Shenxin 3,500 dan, Gengfeng 3,100 dan, Tonghe 8,100 dan, and Yuanda 2,600 dan. Gengfeng bought 6,900 dan, Yuanda 3,100 dan, Tongfu 2,000 dan, Xiesheng 3,100 dan, and Xincheng 4,200 dan. The closing prices are listed below:

Grain Futures Advance Sharply in the Afternoon 231

│Dalian Merchants Continue to Purchase 100,000 Bags of Spot and Forward Flour for January 10th Delivery│

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market, prices for various months were generally stable. The quoted price of foreign wheat was slightly better, by a few cents or fractions of a dime, and both buyers and sellers mostly watched. Although the factories had a lot of foreign wheat chips, they were not very eager to sell, so the prices in each session stabilized. Until the opening in the afternoon, prices for the current month to March advanced sharply. Spot flour sales remained good, and Dalian merchants were very active. Yesterday, they also completed the purchase of 100,000 bags of spot and forward flour for January 10th delivery, at a price of 1 tael 9 dimes 2 and a half cents. As a result, confidence was rekindled, and buying interest was strong. The market from this month to March is exceptionally good. (Rumor has it that Dalian merchants have successively completed orders for about 600,000 to 700,000 bags of spot and forward flour. Due to factories still hedging in April and May, confidence has eased. After observing the follow-up, the tightness of spot flour may require a further increase in the near future. As a result, the current month rose by 2 cents compared to the previous day, January rose by 2 cents and 2.5 li, February rose by 1.5 cents, March rose by 1 cent and 7 li, April rose by 2.5 li, and May rose by 5 li.)

Wheat Market Slightly Soft 232

Yesterday, the forward wheat market was flat and weak. The quoted price of foreign wheat, Canadian wheat, was slightly lower by one or two dimes. Although Chicago was slightly better by a few cents, it was very small. And because foreign wheat has been falling slightly for several days, the wheat market has been inactive, and traders' hedging has been active. Although the volume was not smooth, it seemed better than nothing. Therefore, confidence was slightly soft. However, there were few transactions in the current month and January, and no trading occurred. If traders continue to transact foreign wheat in the follow-up, hedging business may be smooth. As a result, there was no comparison for the current month and January, and February, March, and April were each down by 2 cents, and there was no comparison for May.

Chicago Wheat Shows Mixed Fluctuations 233

Chicago wheat on Thursday initially rose due to Eastern purchases, but later fell due to the weakness of Winnipeg wheat. As a result, the results varied. On the 14th, the transaction volume totaled 10 million bushels. The market prices for the 15th are listed on the left.

Closing Price Compared to Previous Day

Silk and Tea

Raw Silk Transactions Rely Only on French Firms 234

丨American Firms Completely Stalled

Transactions with American firms have completely stalled because the silk price has fallen by another 2 cents. Moreover, Chinese merchants are sticking to their bottom line and are unwilling to budge, so the prices quoted by foreign telegrams are very different, and no deals can be reached. Only Huangchuan silk is being traded with French firms. Baichang silk is also affected by the American situation and has not been traded.

Zhenmei Green Tea Sales to Europe are Improving 235

Yesterday, Zhenmei green tea from Wuyuan, Tunxi, Shexian, and other areas was actively purchased by British firms Xiehe, Jinlong, Tianyu, Tianxiang, etc., due to receiving telegrams from Morocco requesting supplies. A total of 2,083 boxes were traded in the city, and transactions were quite brisk. Currently, Jinlong, Jardine Matheson, and other firms have sent out large batches of Zhenmei telegrams. The general tea merchants and viewers expect the Zhenmei market to rebound. The Russian Aid Society also purchased a large quantity of Qimen black tea, 2,000 to 3,000 boxes, but the quoted price of 36 to 37 taels was too low, the silver payment period was too slow, and the conditions were too difficult to accept.

New Chaoqing Sugar Arrives Again 236

丨Number Plates Expanded and Held, Not Yet Opened丨Coarse Sand White Slightly Lower丨

Yesterday, the sugar market was slightly flat due to the rise in the gold standard. The guild set the price for number 24 coarse sand white at 15 taels 4 dimes and 7.5 cents, and some transactions occurred, only slightly lower by 2.5 cents compared to the previous day (14th). Changxing Firm offered 900 bags of number 18 middle-grade white sugar at a price of 14 taels 3 dimes and 2.5 cents, slightly lower by 2.5 cents compared to the previous day's set price. High-quality number 20 middle-grade sand white was sold out, and numbers 80, 90, and 100 Dutch red sugar remained mostly unchanged and lacked transactions. Chao merchants offered over 100 bags of lower-quality Mianhu red sugar at prices ranging from 10 taels 07 cents to 08 cents. Yesterday, it was reported that the Hesheng wheel had imported a new shipment of 2,890+ bags of Chaoqing sugar. Since there are bound to be even more shipments in the future, this newspaper has long predicted that the market price will inevitably fall. However, due to cost considerations, the numbered houses will still need to hold out for a considerable period of time before a new price can be determined. Therefore, the goods offered the day before will not be immediately affected.

According to a New York telegram on the 15th, spot goods were down slightly at 0625, at 8 and 3/8ths cents. Futures for December were down slightly at 6 points, January was down slightly at 4 points, March and May were each down by 2 points, and July and September were each down by 3 points. A London telegram reported that December was up by 0.75 points, and March and May were each up by 1.25. Sugar was down slightly, at 8 and a half pence (120 pounds).

Metals

Over 11,000 Boxes of Tinplate Traded 237

Over 11,000 boxes of 90-pound British tinplate, preserved by the Boxer Indemnity Committee, were officially offered yesterday at a price of 10 taels and 09 cents. The purchaser was Yuanchun Metal Shop on North Suzhou Road, and the goods were handled by Hezhong and Tianxiang foreign firms. It is expected that the tinplate market will trend upward from now on.

Number 2 White Lead Sheet Actively Purchased by Tea Merchants 238

Number 2 white lead sheet was actively purchased by tea warehouses yesterday, so over 100 barrels were traded at a price of 25 taels and 5 dimes. The inventory is extremely low, and the market outlook is good. According to a reporter's investigation, the total inventory in the city is only about 760 barrels (486 barrels in outside warehouses and approximately 278 barrels in this warehouse). However, arrivals are extremely limited, and the market is very bullish.

Metal Markets in London and New York 239

"London," 15th cable, copper, tin, lead, and zinc all saw slight gains. Antimony and tungsten were unchanged. "New York" also cabled on the same day, tin showed slight gains, while lead, tungsten, and copper were stable with no changes.

Changsha

On a River Steamer (1) 263

— Shi Heng

This story begins on a Yangtze River steamer.

The river water was usually calm and tranquil, but the hearts of the passengers on the steamer were as restless as waves at sea.

Once, a young man boarded a steamer to go to a certain town upstream on the Yangtze River. His demeanor was extravagant, like that of a wealthy family's son. He booked a first-class cabin for two people.

Another man, in his thirties, seemed to coincidentally share the same room with him. Although this man's attire was also neat, someone with life experience could discern the ferocity in his features. However, his speech was very amiable, and within a few minutes, he had become very familiar with his roommate.

The ship sailed in the heart of the river.

On the deck, three or five passengers who appeared to be merchants stood chatting idly. Among them was an elderly man; one look at his attire was enough to know that he was an experienced traveler. However, this old man was upright, as evidenced by the bright gleam emanating from his eyes.

On the ship, it was as if everyone was in a large family; people easily became friendly. Soon, the extravagant young man also stood on the deck, conversing with the old man.

The old man sized up the wealthy young man, asking as if interrogating a criminal:

"You're a first-time traveler, aren't you?"

The young man indifferently smiled and responded.

"You should be careful," the old man continued. "This road is not easy. Young people often run into trouble."

Saying this, the old man spoke of many unfortunate incidents encountered on Yangtze River steamers and at the docks. Before he finished speaking, the young man's roommate, the middle-aged man, also joined them. He and the old man sized each other up, and the old man smiled at him in greeting, but then excused himself and walked away.

Night fell. The old man lay in his cabin, but it seemed as if something unusual was disturbing his heart. He couldn't fall asleep. His mind vividly and clearly reflected the faces of the fierce-looking middle-aged man and the extravagant young man. He thought to himself:

"This man definitely doesn't seem like a good person. His sharing a room with that young man is probably not coincidental, and he's being so friendly to him. I'm almost sixty years old; my eyes don't deceive me. That young man is in danger; I should help him! Fortunately, I'm in a neighboring room; I can listen carefully for any sounds from their room."

The Bribery Burial Pit 264

— Hua

Wang Honglie, the magistrate of Qiu'an County in Shandong, recently invented a new method for punishing corruption. He ordered the digging of a large pit in front of the county government, naming it the "Bribery Burial Pit." He also promulgated a decree: any official under the county government, from the magistrate down to the lowest employee, found to have accepted bribes, must throw themselves into the pit and bury themselves alive. If this were viewed solely from the perspective of "punishing corruption," it would naturally elicit applause and shouts of "wonderful!" However, if we further examine it from the standpoint of "rule of law," Magistrate Wang's "invention" is not only somewhat "illegal" but also seems to be deliberately toying with human lives.

Originally, the "official precepts" established in China were, as Ah Q would say, "too damn soft!" Despite the deafening calls for "building a clean government," the reality of "bribery being openly practiced" is still everywhere to be seen. As long as there is a "bribe," one can sell official positions, sell the law, and sell favors. This kind of buying and selling behavior has almost dominated the entire Chinese politics. The next step of "bribe" is "extortion," and the reality of extorting every drop of marrow is also everywhere to be seen. Under "bribe" and "extortion," there is no "law," no "government," only the scent of gold and silver, only the faces of demons and the tricks of ghosts. If there could be a large pit in this world to bury all kinds of bribery, to rescue "law" and "government" from piles of gold and silver, it would naturally be a great joy.

However, there will never be such a large pit in this world, and "bribery" is not just a simple "moral problem"; it is closely linked to the socio-economic system and can never be buried by a single pit. Taking a step back, there is still "national law" to punish corruption. Those who should be imprisoned are imprisoned, and those who should be beheaded are beheaded. Instead of handling it according to national law, digging a pit and ordering them to throw themselves in and bury themselves alive may be satisfying, but what about "rule of law"? As long as we close our eyes and silently imagine the tragedy of throwing oneself into the pit and burying oneself, our tongues will involuntarily stick out. Isn't this Magistrate Wang deliberately toying with human lives? Corruption is of course punishable by death, but is toying with human lives forgivable?

However, at present, there are many such "overcorrected" and playful behaviors. As long as you are happy, you can come up with an invention at any time, crack a joke at any time. Who cares?

Chinese and Japanese 265

— Gao Ming

That was on March 4th of this year. At that time, China and Japan had almost stopped fighting. Our 19th Route Army had retreated to places like Changshu. On the evening of March 4th, suddenly there was news that our army had counterattacked and that the Japanese commander Shirakawa had been killed. At this time, the joy of some of our ordinary people was indescribable. Every family set off firecrackers, some people ran to the streets to cheer, and some even sat in cars or streetcars beating drums and gongs. The paper scraps from the firecrackers covered the road an inch or two thick, and the streets were literally packed with people. Some people cheered:

"Shirakawa is dead! Shirakawa is dead!"

Even those modern girls walking alone on the street were smiling. Why? Because Shirakawa was dead.

The Chinese are so lacking in the spirit of "fair play."

Reading the December issue of the Japanese "Shincho" magazine, there is an article by Akie Chikaumatsu entitled "An Outsider's View of the News," in which there is the following passage:

"In early August, I went from Tokyo to Nikko. By the time I arrived in Nikko, it was already evening. The people in this countryside were lined up, carrying lanterns, parading through the streets. I asked them what was going on, and they said that because Ma Zhanshan had died in battle, they were celebrating with lanterns. I couldn't help but smile."

Therefore, we know and are "relieved" that our "civilized" Japanese also lack the spirit of "fair play."

In this day and age, talking about "fair play" may be outdated, or at least a bit Don Quixote-ish. But somehow, this feeling is always endearing.

Rambling Words Facing the Wall 266

— Ye Lingfeng

The moon is overhead.

I walked into the study that I hadn't entered for a long time. A kind of gloomy and stagnant air suddenly aroused a feeling of desolation and sorrow in my heart, making me feel as if I had walked into my own tomb. The joys and sorrows of the past were now quietly covered in the ruthless years.

Ten years of wandering, the remaining light illuminating empty flowers, having experienced all the illusions that young people are infatuated with. After everything has disappeared, only these half-wall of remaining books have left me with indelible traces. Facing each book on this shelf, I can imagine a lonely soul, guarding his own treasure in calm oblivion.

I pulled down a British novel that was popular seven years ago, blew away the dust sleeping on top, and opened the first page. On the yellowed paper, I saw a few lines of faint pencil writing:

"The moon hangs high, urging me to return home, the vast sea and blue sky are both indistinct. Ten years by the lake and sea, I feel much sorrow, again towards the southern sky, I ask what can be done."

Seven years ago, on a chilly early evening, sitting around the crimson fireplace, Li, whose wedding date had been set, took this book I was reading from my hand and left these few sentences on the blank page. She silently handed it to me, I glanced at it, and then quietly closed the book, squatting down to poke at the ashes in the fireplace. My young heart already knew how to cherish its own sorrow at that time, unwilling to give it away lightly.

Returning from walking in the moonlight, feeling the light cold, I chewed on the taste of helplessness that rippled in my heart, never having the courage to open that unfinished book again. Time flies, quietly seven years have passed. In these seven years, I have not had the opportunity to see her again, only indirectly heard from people that she is now flourishing like green leaves, with children in tow. Her virtuous heart has probably long brushed away that accidental gathering and scattering.

Facing these faint traces, holding the book, I stood quietly facing the wall. From the indifference, I was once again drawn into the net that I had woven myself. December 15th.

Strange Tales of Australian Aborigines 267

— Wei

Australia, located in the southwest of the South Pacific islands, is a British-claimed continent. The aborigines there are uncivilized people, divided into tribes, with a headman who dominates the people of each tribe with absolute power. The headman is sometimes hereditary; but usually, rare and exotic natural objects can be used as gifts to buy the position of headman. Among the aborigines, there is a type of person called a doctor. These people act as priests for various tribes, also perform like magicians, and sometimes even casually treat people's illnesses according to their own ideas, so they can indeed be considered useful doctors. The methods used by these doctors are mostly mystical: they use dreams and illusions to predict certain omens. In our view, although it is entirely a figment of the imagination, they believe it is a trick to use magic.

×××××

When a child is born in a tribe, they immediately calculate its fate to see if it can be kept alive. Most of the firstborn children are always killed. Also, if the previous child has not been weaned, then most of the later-born children are killed. (In practice, these children are also difficult to raise to adulthood.) According to statistics from the Australian government, one-third to one-half of newborn children are killed in this muddled way. The reason why some aborigines are willing to make such a sacrifice is because they believe that the killed child can be reborn as a person when the next child is born.

×××××

As for the children who are allowed to survive, they are very much loved. The mother often gives him milk until he is two or three years old; the father coaxes him every day. When the child grows up, the parents use various methods to make him happy. Therefore, the childhood of Australian aborigines is their happiest time. When they are nine or ten years old, this happy time comes to an end; girls, with a simple ceremony, leap into adulthood, and boys, with a more complicated ceremony, leap into adulthood. This ceremony varies from tribe to tribe: the simplest of which is the Kurnai tribe.

×××××

Court Ladies and Prostitutes 268

— Shi Zhecun

I happened to see in the seventh issue of "Art Fortnightly" a reproduction of a work by the great French sculptor Rodin, with a Chinese title translated below as "Beautiful Old Court Lady." I couldn't help but slap the table in surprise. I don't remember Rodin ever doing a statue for any court lady. I have known this reproduced statue for a long time; it is Rodin's masterpiece, entitled "Beautiful Heaulmiere." Rodin created this strangely ugly statue entirely based on a poem by the ancient French poet Villon, "The Lament of the Beautiful Heaulmiere." Indeed, under the statue reproduced in "Art Fortnightly" was also noted a line "See translated poem in the fifth issue," so I went to find the fifth issue of "Art Fortnightly" and found a Chinese translation of Villon's poem on page seven. But the title was still "Beautiful Old Court Lady."

The word Heaulmiere comes from the word Heaulme. Heaulme is a kind of helmet in ancient times, Heaulmere can be translated as helmet maker! Ieaulmiere is the meaning of helmet maker's wife. This beautiful helmet maker's wife is a prostitute, a character in the French classical literature "Romance of the Rose." The poet Villon lamented the passing of youth and the impermanence of beauty, so he imagined this woman, who was once famous for her beauty, lamenting her fading beauty thirty years after her husband's death, turning into extremely poignant lyrics.

The gist of the first section of this poem is "I think I heard the beautiful woman who used to be the helmet maker's wife, she is regretting her youth, ah! Old age, cruel old age, why did you destroy my appearance so quickly? What else is there to miss, that makes me not want to kill myself." Singing to this point, the elderly beauty looked at her shrunken skin and withered arms, and couldn't help but recall the snowy skin and flower-like face of the past. So the gist of the second section onwards is "Ah, he has been dead for more than thirty years, now only I am left, an old woman. I think about the good old days; how beautiful I was then. How am I now, when I look at my naked body, the appearance is much thinner, withered, weak and trembling, I am really furious. Where has my soft, smooth forehead gone? Where have my golden hair and beautiful eyes gone? Where has my moderate nose gone? Where have my small ears, my delicate face, my vermilion lips gone?" The following are two sections of poems that try their best to describe an aging prostitute, singing in sequence, the shoulders, arms, eyebrows, eyes, nose, limbs, breasts are all gaunt, dry, withered, shrunken, and dull. "This is the end of human beauty!" In the last section, the poet wrote such a warning.

The sculptor Rodin specifically used the appearance described in this poem as a blueprint to create his masterpiece. We should naturally read Villon's poem while carefully looking at Rodin's sculpture. It is easy to appreciate the advantages of the expression methods of these two arts. Unfortunately, "Art Fortnightly" did not translate the entire original poem, and Rodin's works cannot be seen in China. These are inevitably some shortcomings. As for translating both titles as court ladies, that is completely irrelevant.

Long Creative Work

Crossroads of Era and Love Seventeen 269

— Zhang Ziping

He was drinking milk when he saw Madam Hezi also carrying a cup of milk, biting a piece of bread, walking up with a smile on her face.

"Mr. Lin, is there too little bread?"

"No."

"Mr. Lin must not be happy eating breakfast alone. That's why I came up to accompany you to eat together. May I?"

He tilted his head slightly and said with a smile.

"You have guests; you should go down and accompany them."

Haiquan wanted to say a few more blunt words to satirize her. But he couldn't think of any at the moment. Some were too harsh, for fear of provoking her anger.

"Is there enough milk to drink?"

"I have more here."

"Have more? Let me drink it?"

"Aren't you going to drink it?"

Madam Hezi really walked over, picked up his milk cup, took two sips, and put it back.

"Mr. Lin, why don't you have any smile today? I won't go down until I see you smile."

After she said this, he couldn't help but smile.

"Please finish drinking that cup of milk."

"No."

"You really are an interesting child! Mr. Lin, please come early after school today, lest I look forward to you. Don't be as late as last night."

As she spoke, she went downstairs. Seeing her leave, Haiquan felt like he had lost something.

He closed his room door, carrying his schoolbag, just about to go downstairs when he suddenly saw the nanny bring up an invitation. He took it and looked at it; it was:

A modest vegetarian feast will be served at five o'clock in the afternoon on December 5th.

Sincerely,

Ren Jinhua Liu Peizhen

Residence: 45, Lane H, Avenue Joffre

(Nine)

Haiquan looked at the invitation again and again, as if wanting to find some means of revenge against Madam Hezi from this invitation, also like wanting to seek cheerleaders from this invitation, because he felt like he was on stage, and soon he would start wrestling with that oriental wearing a Japanese kimono. Who would be his backup.

"Should I take this invitation with me, or leave it at home?"

He hesitated greatly for this question. At the same time, he hoped to see Madam Hezi come down from upstairs, so that he could show her this invitation, as a demonstration. But he waited for a while and still didn't see Madam Hezi come down. Seeing that the time for class was approaching, he gave the invitation to the nanny.

Extra Edition of Shen Bao for Local News

Talk

Prosperous Cities 270

— Wen Bing

I am not absolutely opposed to prosperous cities, I just feel that the countryside should not be forgotten either. China is founded on agriculture, and has not paid much attention to industrial and commercial cities since ancient times, so that the practice of rural market fairs prevailed in past dynasties, gathering commodities at a certain suitable location at a set time for trading. According to Mayor Wu, municipal administration in China began in Guangzhou, in February 15, 1921, when the Guangdong Provincial Government promulgated the Provisional Regulations for Guangzhou City, dividing it into municipal administrative districts. It can also be seen that it is only recently that our country has paid attention to the prosperity and facilities of cities, which is quite lamentable.

Recently, the people of our country have paid great attention to the prosperity of cities. A few days ago, I read Mayor Wu's speech on Greater Shanghai, which aroused deep illusions in me. Yesterday, I also saw in the newspaper that the Beijing Municipal Government had drafted a plan to prosper the city of Beijing, and had submitted the plan to the central government for approval. The outline is divided into nine items, including society, public security, and property. The Guangdong Provincial Government has also drafted a new plan to prosper the Guangzhou urban area, designating Dashatou as a commercial development area, saying that to seek prosperity, entertainment venues must first be equipped, and to develop entertainment venues, smoking rooms, gambling halls, and brothels must first be ordered to relocate, with heavy taxes levied on violators. It is said to be an excellent method of discouraging through taxation, which made me sigh with admiration after reading it.

Standing on the position of prosperous cities, I express my approval of the Greater Shanghai Plan and the Plan to Prosper Beijing. However, the plan of Guangdong to prosper the urban area is no different from publicly advocating that people learn to smoke, gamble, and prostitute. I can only wait and see the future, and I dare not agree rashly for the time being.

However, I still have a further point to say, that is, we should not completely forget the countryside for the sake of prosperous cities! I know that China's cities are not as prosperous as those in Europe and the United States. Not to mention the smaller ones, even the top-notch Shanghai, Beijing, and Guangzhou are still ashamed in many ways, and it is indeed necessary to quickly prosper, but it must be known that cities are just a microcosm of the countryside, a concentration of rural agricultural products and an economic hub. In the final analysis, it should start with the prosperity of the countryside. Our country has a natural environment of vast land and sparse population, and a mild climate. Since ancient times, it has been famous as an agricultural country, producing rice, tea, silk, and other products, which not only provides for its own use, but also sells a large amount overseas. Tea, silk, and porcelain have always held the world's leading position. Among the grains, the soybeans of the Northeast have also been exported in large quantities, which is not uncommon for a wealthy national economy.

Now, foreign tea merchants barely dare accept it, and exports have almost disappeared. The right to silkworm silk has been given to the slave country to seize. The porcelain of Jiangxi is not much exported either. What is most distressing is that food has actually occupied the top position in imported goods. Alas, China founded on agriculture, how can this be endured.

There are many reasons for the bankruptcy of the countryside. The political system is not on track, the forces of international capitalism have penetrated into the countryside, bandits are rampant, and natural disasters are frequent, all of which are the main reasons. However, most people only care about running towards the city, and the government only cares about the prosperity of the city, resulting in a chaotic situation of priorities and the increasing poverty of society. This can also be regarded as one of the biggest causes of rural bankruptcy! Therefore, after reading the prosperity plans of the three major cities of Shanghai, Beijing, and Guangzhou, I can't help but have some feelings, and now I want to shout.

"Don't forget the countryside when prospering cities."

Common Sense

The Method of Making Blueprint Paper 271

— Er Ming

In recent years, engineering and construction have been developing rapidly, and the art of drawing and planning has also become increasingly popular. Each project requires several copies of drawings, and many require dozens or hundreds of copies. Manual copying is impossible, and stone printing is too expensive. Therefore, blueprint paper has become a necessity in modern engineering and construction. In addition, universities with engineering and technical schools, railway bureaus, and water conservancy bureaus, as well as photography, all rely heavily on this paper. However, the manufacturing of blueprint paper is not difficult, and I will describe it below.

Preparation of the Blueprint Paper Solution: This paper requires two solutions to be mixed together. ㈠ Potassium Ferricyanide Solution, also known as Red Prussiate of Potash deep liquid. ㈡ Ammonium Ferric Citrate Solution, also known as deep liquid of Ammonia and Iron Citrate.

For the usual preparation of these two salt solutions, dissolve them separately and then combine them. The first chemical should be ground into a fine powder. The second chemical is usually in pure form and dissolves easily. It can become solid at all times, but it dissolves when exposed to moisture. After a few days, it softens and becomes unusable. Therefore, the amount of this chemical to be prepared should be determined by the amount to be used (must be prepared in a dark room).

Amount of Dissolution and Combination: There are different methods for combining, but the most suitable amounts are as follows:

First Solution: One ounce of Red Prussiate of Potash (equivalent to 7.61 qian in Kuping weight) and six ounces of water, or two and a half ounces of Red Prussiate of Potash and one pint of water (equivalent to 0.61 liters, weighing approximately 12.67 liang). After this liquid is completely dissolved, filter it (using raw cotton for speed).

Second Solution: One and a half ounces of Ammonium Ferric Citrate and six ounces of water, or four ounces of Iron Citrate and one pint of water. After this liquid is completely dissolved, it must also be filtered until it is very clear. The first and second solutions should be stored separately in glass bottles with glass stoppers and placed in a dark room for use. When using, combine the two liquids in equal parts and filter again carefully to prevent any Red Prussiate of Potash powder from remaining in the liquid. If this mixed liquid changes from brown to light blue-green, it should not be used. Every four ounces of this mixed solution can be used to make paper with an area of one hundred square feet, costing only one or two jiao in洋.

Paper Material for Making Blueprint Paper: Ordinary paper that is strong and washable is sufficient. For printing fine drawings, paper that is fine, strong, smooth, and uniform, and that the solution cannot penetrate through to the back, is preferable. Otherwise, the liquid will penetrate the paper and cause a chemical reaction, and the image will not appear even after washing. German Saxe paper and French Rives paper are excellent for making this type of paper. Other high-quality options include Weston's and Scottish Seoteh's linen paper, which have the tightest texture. All of the above papers must be imported from foreign countries, and our country does not have them, which is truly regrettable. However, if there are domestically made papers that are strong and smooth, a small amount can be tested. If good results are obtained, it can be used as a substitute.

Order of Dyeing Paper with Solution: Dyeing paper with the solution must be done in a dark room. The so-called dark room does not have to be completely dark, but it must have a slight amount of light or a square of red glass embedded in the wall to allow light to pass through. The solution only needs to dye one side of the paper. There are two methods of applying the dye, which are described below:

㈠ Floating Dyeing Method: Place the solution in a large, shallow basin with a flat bottom. Float the paper on the surface of the liquid, with the front side of the paper touching the solution. When floating the paper, hold two opposite corners of the paper with both hands so that the other two opposite corners touch the surface of the liquid. Lower one of the held corners first, then lower the other. After the entire paper touches the liquid, flip half of the paper over to check for air bubbles. If there are any, re-touch the paper to the surface of the liquid and drag it from side to side. The half without air bubbles can be flipped up and does not need to touch the liquid. After the entire paper has been floating on the liquid surface for about one or two minutes, it can be taken out and hung next to the water basin to allow the remaining liquid to drain away. The result of this method is good, and it all depends on the skill of the operation. The shallow square basin used for dyeing paper must be larger than the paper being dyed, and there must be room for movement around it. The inside of the basin must not only be leak-proof but also resistant to chemical reactions to be considered good.

㈡ Brush Dyeing Method: Lay the paper flat on a flat board, with a soft, smooth oilcloth between the paper and the board. Dip a wide, soft brush into the solution and evenly brush the surface of the paper, repeating two or three times. This method

Page 20

is the simplest, but it must be done quickly. If one side is not dyed and the other side is already dry, then this paper is useless. If dyeing long and large paper, two people are required. First, use a wet brush to quickly dye the paper once, then use a light brush to brush across the surface of the paper to squeeze out the wet water, and then apply the liquid so that it is deeply and evenly spread. Rapid dyeing can achieve good results. After the dyeing is complete, clamp one side of the paper to a horizontal pole and hang it in a dark room to dry.

Preservation of Blueprint Paper: After the paper is made, it must be carefully stored in a dark and dry place. Small ones should be placed flat in wooden or paper boxes, and large ones should be rolled up and stored in paper or lead tubes, etc., covered and sealed to prevent decay for a long time. The finished paper must never be folded. Once folded, the surface of the paper will be uneven and unusable.

A "Non-Verbose" Letter 272

— Yin Ming

There was an old scholar who went to the capital to take the exam. Every time he wrote a letter to his wife, the wording was very "verbose." His wife therefore wrote a letter to him, telling him not to be "verbose" in his letters in the future. He then concentrated on writing a "non-verbose" letter. His letter is as follows:

In the past, I was verbose, but today I will no longer be verbose. Verbose language is annoying, so I have deleted it.

The newly built city gate tower in Nanjing has wind chimes on all four corners. The wind makes them ring loudly, ding-ding-dang-dang, dang-dang-ding-ding, which is very different from the guest room in our house.

If I pass the exam this time, then you will be a madam, the eldest son will be the eldest young master, the second son will be the second young master, the third son will be the third young master, the fourth son will be the fourth young master, and the fifth son will be the fifth young master; if I do not pass the exam, then you will still be a wife, the eldest son will still be the eldest son, the second son will still be the second son, the third son will still be the third son, the fourth son will still be the fourth son, and the fifth son will still be the fifth son. There is a pair of cotton shoes in the box. Take them out to dry in the sun, beat them, and pat them. Pat them and beat them to prepare for the cold weather.

When your period comes, be sure not to stand outside the door and be seen by Wang Er Mazi across the street, lest he have bad intentions. A thousand times, ten thousand times, in my haste, I didn't have time to write the "cao" (草) radical, so I used a big square with a dot removed to represent it.

Shop Employees' Correspondence

Suggestions for Solving Reading Problems 273

Editor:

I am not a shop employee, and I am not very clear about the lives of shop employees. Recently, after reading your "Shop Employees' Correspondence," it aroused my sympathy for the suffering of shop employees.

Today (December 14), you raised four questions, asking everyone to express their opinions; I am a teacher, so I will talk about the second question.

"How can shop employees, apprentices, and trainees satisfy their desire for knowledge?"

I think: For this question, if the following method is adopted, a considerable solution can definitely be obtained at present. What method?

"Organize shop employees' reading clubs by shop employees, apprentices, and trainees who are aspiring to improve. Create a mobile library by the reading club."

Now let me explain why this method should be used:

First, because shop employees have very little time to read every day: to reduce the time spent running around borrowing and returning books, the only way is to create a mobile library.

Second, because the libraries that already exist in Shanghai at present, the books inside are not specially equipped for shop employees, nor are they equipped based on the actual needs of shop employees.

Those that meet the actual needs of shop employees are also plagued by too few books, making it inconvenient to circulate. Therefore, it is best for shop employees to create a mobile library that they really need themselves.

Third, to create a mobile library, money is essential. However, if this is done by one person, it will naturally be difficult; if it is done by many people, it will be an easy task. Therefore, it is necessary to first organize reading clubs by shop employees, and then set up libraries.

The above is the result of my thinking at the moment, and naturally the thinking cannot be thorough. For example, the following questions have not been adequately resolved:

㈠ How to obtain reading time for shop employees?

㈡ What is the internal organization of the reading club?

㈢ What is the internal organization of the library?

However, I think these questions should not be discussed in too much detail for the time being. The most important thing now is:

"Just organize with two or three people!"

Because only after organizing will methods that meet the public will be produced! Only methods that are publicly recognized are possible!

Editor! What do you think?

Shop employees, apprentices, and trainees! What do you think?

Zhang Jianhua, December 14

Editor's Note: Mr. Zhang believes that to satisfy the desire for knowledge of shop employees, it is necessary to establish a mobile library. This question is precisely what we have been constantly concerned about and have already obtained a satisfactory solution.

To commemorate the 60th anniversary of the founding of our newspaper, we have specially established a circulating library on the third floor, numbers 345, of the Continental Shopping Mall on Nanjing Road, a commercially central location with convenient transportation, with the primary purpose of supporting industrial and commercial education. Therefore, the three questions raised by Mr. Zhang have all been easily solved.

㈠ The library has a delivery method: employees are hired to deliver books directly to the borrowers' places, free of charge. Shop employees can sit in the shop all day and still have ample opportunity to borrow books.

㈡ At the beginning of the library's opening, an announcement was published on the cover of our newspaper: readers are welcome to inform us at any time of the names and publishing locations of their favorite books so that we can purchase them. This will ensure that the books placed in the library can meet the needs of shop employees.

㈢ The economic aspect is entirely the responsibility of our newspaper, so there is naturally no problem.

As for the question of the shop employees' reading club, it is best for the shop employees themselves to come up with a solution, and we are very willing to do our best to support them. Moreover, we very much agree with Mr. Zhang's suggestion regarding the scope of the organization of this type of club. The number of people does not need to be large, and three or four people can organize it (in fact, the number of people should not be too large). It seems that this is not an impossible task, and we are very willing to hear news of such an organization among the readers as soon as possible to solve our intellectual hunger and depression.
