Nickname 275

— Ming Ming

It was about Monday morning, after the memorial week was over, followed by the unbearably noisy Chinese class.

Before long, the class bell rang, and after five minutes, the students outside the classroom slowly entered the dull classroom one by one. Suddenly, the sound of leather shoes clattering outside the classroom reached our classroom. Looking up, "Ha!" The classmates in the classroom shouted in unison, and even the students with nearsightedness quickly took out their glasses and put them on their noses to see what was happening.

It turned out that the Chinese teacher, who usually loved simplicity, had completely changed his attire today. He was wearing a red-knotted melon-skin hat on his head, a green silk cotton robe on his body, and a large floral satin mandarin jacket on top. The cloth-bottomed shoes he brought from the countryside were also gone, and he was actually wearing clattering leather shoes. Looking at these half-new and half-old leather shoes, he had never worn them before. They were probably淘 from the famous old goods market in Shanghai. So, among the students, there was one nicknamed Little Monkey, known for his mischievousness. Seeing the Chinese teacher's rural modernized appearance today, he gave him a nickname called "Little Tang Ming." The whole class burst into laughter again.

Amidst the students' loud laughter and commotion, the teacher opened the register and began to call names. He used all the strength he had when he was breastfeeding as a child to finish calling the names of more than forty people. As a result, everyone was present, even the sick student who had not gotten out of bed for a long time was there today. The teacher, regardless of anything, opened the textbook and began to explain the page that had not been finished last time. In this always disliked Chinese class, who would listen? So, some were holding pens and bowing their heads writing love letters, some were looking at pictures of their loved ones, and some were holding pens and filling them with ink, writing complaints in the newspaper. In this class, there was everything imaginable.

The teacher, who was called Little Tang Ming, explained with relish, shaking his head and swaying his tail, expressing his criticisms and opinions. Later, it became too noisy, making the "Little Tang Ming" teacher jump up and put the red-knotted hat on his head on the podium. This release caused the whole class of students to laugh wildly again. Just when things were in this awkward state, suddenly the life-saving bell rang. So the teacher shouted loudly, saying, "I'll spare you this time, but you must never do this again." He immediately put on his hat, grabbed his books, and ran away. So the students all shouted in unison, "One...Two...Three, Little Tang Ming..."

Novel

Writing a Letter to a Friend's Wife (Continued 9) 276

— Qin Shouou

Just because of watching this scene, I was delayed, so that even though I took the night train, there were no sleeping cars available; I had no choice but to put my sick body, which I had barely managed to get out of bed, into an ordinary first-class carriage. But unexpectedly, this one mistake allowed me, after abandoning everything, to encounter an unexpected adventure.

Beautiful little darling! What kind of adventure do you think it was? Could there be anyone besides you worth me calling an adventure? No! No! It was just too coincidental, which is why I called it an adventure.

As I stepped into the carriage, I sat down very quickly on a single seat as if I had a case of hypochondria. I immediately hid my head in my raised coat collar, cowering in a corner. I didn't distinguish clearly what kind of people were sitting around me, whether they were men, women, old, or young. I just felt that they were all people.

"Hi! Mr. Zhu!" The car had been running for three or four minutes when a very crisp and familiar voice suddenly spoke very fluently directly across from me: at the same time, five very slender fingers boldly pulled open the coat collar that was covering my face.

This very ordinary little action caused me a great shock, as if I had encountered some kind of major change, and I almost jumped up from my seat. My eyes, as if annoyed, stared round and wide, but the shadow of the person only two feet away from me was still very blurry.

Ah, dear little brother, to tell you the truth: if a timid friend had seen my condition at that time, he might have sent me to the International Funeral Home immediately.

"Hi! Mr. Zhu! Are you sick?" The person sitting across from me, who first greeted me, also immediately noticed that I was sick.

Although he had already called the word "Mr." followed by my surname very clearly twice in the tone of an American gentleman, I still couldn't remember which close friend he was. However, I had already recognized clearly that she was a she, not a he.

Thankfully, someone with courage in the back opened a glass window, regardless of public opinion, allowing the sharp and fierce night wind to rush into the carriage one after another. I happened to be right in the line of fire, and the wind swirled around the back of my neck: before long, I was already shivering, and my head became clear. Immediately, a lady appeared before me, so modernized that others couldn't tell whether she was a prostitute or a virtuous woman. Red rouge, white powder, and green黛 had joined forces to cover her true face; a杏yellow silk旗pao was so tight that it seemed to be one with her flesh, revealing her curves as much as possible; and she was wearing a foreign wool spring coat on her back that was not practical but only for decoration.

After all, who is she? This person is not only someone you would never guess; even I almost thought it wasn't real in the first five minutes. Because she came so unexpectedly!

Don't worry, dear little brother, let me tell you! She is none other than your Lawyer Zhou's old lover丨丨Miss Li Fang. Isn't that strange?

Even stranger is that ever since this dear classmate of ours left school and heartlessly abandoned Da Jing, although I had a childishly ridiculous idea of finding her and scolding her thoroughly, I had never encountered her. Who would have thought that at this final juncture, we would meet face to face as if by some ghostly trick.

Joan Crawford's Secret to Success 277

— Jia Nan

Joan Crawford, Mrs. Fanpengke, who has returned from her trip to Europe, is now very different from before. She has been embraced by the people of the United States, occupying one of the top ten stars in Hollywood, and for several years, the mysterious queen of嘉賓 has been trending to relinquish her寶座, for sure. The current Joan Crawford has reached the peak of success, but the success of a career is by no means accidental. She has a beautiful face, a moderate figure, and wonderful eyebrows, and a square and broad mouth, many features. She has嘉賓's mystery, but these are not the key to her success.

Therefore, she has always maintained a modest and self-effacing attitude towards any reporter's interview.

She is not only polite to reporters, but she is also very polite to everyone, so no one in Hollywood dislikes being close to her. She and her husband, Mr. Fanpengke, have never had a conflict, and they still maintain the honor of being a "model couple" in Hollywood.

Dutch Cinemas Do Not Admit Children 280

— Yun

Dutch children are not as lucky as children in our country. Because cinemas there seem to be places for adults to spend their time, ordinary films are absolutely prohibited for children under the age of eighteen to visit. However, this is a rule set by their government, not like some cinemas in Shanghai, which use the prohibition of children to visit as advertising. Sometimes when Dutch cinemas encounter films that are specially allowed for children to visit, the cinemas will advertise them widely, and the children are all very happy because they see movies too few times, only three or four times a year!

New Movie Introduction

General Yan's Bitter Tea (Part 2) 281

— Crane

Thunderbolt from a Clear Sky: Because of Mary's collusion with the enemy, the enemy forces at the front line suddenly gained an advantage, and a huge amount of public grain was seized by them. General Yan thus encountered difficulties both militarily and economically. The soldiers lacked morale, and the main forces retreated in disarray.

General Yan was defeated. Megau wanted to leave with him, but he told her to go first, because even if he were captured by his enemies, she could escape safely.

Farewell! Megan got into the plank boat, but General Yan stood still on the shore, holding a gun in his hand, waving and telling the sailors to set sail. The shouts of the rebel soldiers grew closer, and Megan was almost driven mad with fear.

General Yan sacrificed his own life to save a foreign girlfriend whom he respected.

In this way, the leaders of the internal strife can rest assured, because this film does not bring out their individuality, but portrays them as gentle, affectionate heroes.

As for the civil war, it is of course depicted accurately, with the flames of war, tragic cries, and refuge-seeking, but all of these are unique products of China, to which we are accustomed. Moreover, with such an affectionate general, perhaps it can correct foreigners' impression of the cruel and tyrannical warlords of our country. The remaining scenes of poetic moonlit nights and the sweet nothings whispered between the hero and the beautiful woman are even more thought-provoking.

Of course, there are also shortcomings, such as General Yan wearing a robe-like outer garment at home, and Mary's clothing being completely out of step with modern Chinese women today. In addition, the government offices that look like vegetable decorations and the large-scale bombing by aircraft, which have never been used in any internal war, are inevitably criticized for being unrealistic or superfluous. The most regrettable thing is that they did not use Chinese-American actresses such as Anna May Wong or Violet Wong to play Mary Corner, but instead used Toshi Mori, a Japanese Tokyo Sakura Girl. She has no knowledge of China, which makes her completely out of character, and the whole film is inferior because of it.

Finally, I earnestly implore the Film Censorship Board not to prohibit the screening of this excellent film in China, so that we can all feast our eyes and see this affectionate General Yan. Even if not, we can also see whether the Americans' impression of China has improved at all. (End)

Film Review of National Films

"Tears of Red in the Empty Gate" 282

— Gu Yan

This is a masterpiece from the silent era of Tianyi (Film Company). I never expected it to be released at this time.

Plot

It tells the story of a woman who is oppressed and powerless to resist, who is forced by the dark society to take refuge in Buddhism, lightly and easily sacrificing a lifetime of happiness in a nunnery. In terms of the times, this is an outdated work, but in the sincere mind of the character Xiuhua, because of her situation and education, she naturally cannot think of a better refuge. Modern women would all think her thinking is backward. Apart from this small point, when we combine the plot of the entire drama, although it is not very good, it can be considered a good production in the silent era of Tianyi. Because it was produced last spring.

Director

There are many ideas, but there are also many places where it imitates foreign films, but the application is not forced. It seems that in the scene where Chen Yumei is hit by a car, she lies too unnaturally. It does not look like she was knocked down and lying there. This is some carelessness. When Sun Min and Chen Yumei return from the hospital, they seem to have been home for a long time, because Sun Min changed into a blue suit, and Yumei's pigtails became a fan-shaped bun. This is a small point of negligence. In addition, scenes such as Xiao Zhengzhong and Ma Dongwu's hair turning white in one shot all lack careful explanation.

Performance

Chen Yumei is very ordinary in the first half and very delicate in the second half. Shu Lijuan is naturally good at playing fierce women, and she does it more crisply in this film than in "Little Actress." Sun Min cannot find any wonderful parts, but he is very steady. Zhang Zhenduo and Qin Haha love to act too much, so they inevitably have the problem of "inserting candles" in civilized dramas. Ge Fu's performance is most suitable for the identity. Jiang Naifang and Xu Jingzhen can act according to their personality. Ma Dongwu and Xiao Zhengzhong have no major flaws, but the male disguise as a female is a bit nauseating.

Makeup

Chen Yumei is the best. She can clearly distinguish the times. Ma Dongwu's face is also very natural.

Photography

The technique is not bad. "Change" and "composite printing" are very clean, but the light is too strong and the reflection is dazzling, which is very annoying.

Scenery 283

The nunnery and the small street scene are very realistic in these two scenes, especially the road and alley in a heavy snowstorm, which are perfectly arranged, and the rest are ordinary. Conclusion In summary of the above points, it cannot be said that this is not a progressive work by Tianyi. Flaws are inevitable in any work, but I hope that the people of Tianyi will work hard as much as possible. Chen Yumei's nickname Yun Tianyi's Chen Yumei, her nickname is called "Bao Bao." When she first entered the film industry, she worked as an actor at the Dongfang Film Company founded by Mr. Zhang Boren, and at that time she was called "Chen Linfeng." Later, she was appreciated by Shao Zuiweng, the general manager of Tianyi Company, and joined Tianyi Company, and changed her name to "Yumei." After Mr. Shao's efforts to promote her, she is now the mainstay of Tianyi Company. Film Treatise "Playing False as Real" Chen Dabei I have said earlier that we Chinese people, because of our complex bloodline, have a naturally stronger ability to imitate than people of pure blood. Therefore, we should have the greatest contribution in the art of performance. But the fact is just the opposite. Why is that? In my opinion, this is because we are not good at practicing the four words "playing false as real." Europeans and Americans surpass us in the most obvious place, which is that they are good at "playing false as real." This is not only the case on the stage and on the screen, but even in daily life, they can make every play that they know is false come alive as if it were real. People who live in Shanghai only need to take a look at a foreigner's funeral, and then take a look at a Chinese person's funeral, and they will understand. You see, almost every relative and friend at their funerals can fully express a kind of sadness on their faces. The relatives and friends at our Chinese funerals hold a stick of incense in their hands, and their mouths are either biting on a cigarette or chattering and laughing with their companions, almost forgetting what they are doing on the road. Then compare the solemn atmosphere in their churches with the pairs of sly eyes of the monks and Taoists who set off fireworks in our streets and alleys. In this kind of thing, no matter which world you run into, you can find some evidence that our people are not good at "playing false as real." Why is the performing arts of Europe and the United States so developed? It is because they have opportunities to practice "playing false as real" everywhere away from the stage, because they perform their plays greatly in social life.
